8 min
Consideration of Concept in Non-Shar'i Speech
Rule that concept is valid in non-Shar'i contexts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the contexts in which mafhum al-mukhalafa is considered valid in the Hanafi school and apply the rule to examples from custom, transactions, narrations, and rational matters.

Core Idea
Mafhum al-mukhalafa is valid everywhere except in the direct speech of the Lawgiver.

This lesson clarifies a crucial methodological rule for muftis: when can you rely on the implied opposite meaning (mafhum al-mukhalafa) of a statement? The source distinguishes between the speech of the Lawgiver (Quran and hadith) and all other contexts—people's custom, transactions, rational arguments, and narrations from mujtahids. Understanding this distinction is essential for proper istidlal and fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core distinction
Read the first part of the passage which states that specifying something by mention does not indicate negation in the addresses of the Lawgiver, but does indicate in people's custom and transactions. Understand that this is the foundational rule.
2
Examine the acknowledgment example
Consider the statement 'You do not owe me more than one hundred dirhams.' According to the rule, this is an acknowledgment of exactly one hundred, as the mafhum excludes amounts above (and below). This shows how mafhum operates in everyday speech.
3
Apply the refinement for narrations and Companion statements
Note that mafhum is valid in narrations from mujtahids (riwayat) by agreement, but not in the texts of revelation (nusus). However, Companion statements that are not based on opinion are treated as marfu' and thus fall under Shar'i speech, so mafhum is not considered there.
4
Resolve the apparent contradiction with al-Ashbah
The passage mentions that al-Ashbah says concept is not allowed in people's speech, but later scholars reconciled this: the prohibition refers to using concept as primary evidence, not as an indicator. The relied-upon position is that mafhum is valid in non-Shar'i contexts.

قال في شرح التحرير بعد قوله غير معتبر في كلام الشارع فقط: فقد نقل الشيخ جلال الدين الخبازي في حاشية "الهداية" عن شمس الأئمة الكردري: "أن تخصيص الشيء بالذكر لا يدل على نفي الحكم عما عداه في خطابات الشارع فأما في متفاهم الناس وعرفهم، وفي المعاملات والعقليات يدل. وتداوله المتأخرون، وعليه ما في "خزانة الأكمل" و"الخانية". لو قال: "ما لك عليّ أكثر من مائة درهم" كان إقرارا بالمائة، ولا يشكل عليه عدم لزوم شيء في "ما لك علي أكثر من مائة درهم ولا أقل"، كما لا يخفى على المتأمل.

He said in Sharh al-Tahrir after his statement 'not considered in the speech of the Lawgiver only': Indeed, Shaykh Jalal al-Din al-Khazzazi transmitted in his gloss on al-Hidayah from Shams al-A'imma al-Kardari: 'That specifying something by mention does not indicate the negation of the ruling from what is other than it in the addresses of the Lawgiver. As for in people's mutual understanding and custom, and in transactions and rational matters, it does indicate. And the later scholars adopted it, and upon it is what is in Khizanat al-Akmal and al-Khaniyya. If one says: 'You do not owe me more than one hundred dirhams,' it is an acknowledgement of one hundred, and it is not problematic that nothing is due in 'You do not owe me more than one hundred dirhams nor less,' as is not hidden from the one who reflects. And from it are the statements of al-Nahr: The concept is considered in narrations by agreement, and in the verdicts of the Companions. He said: It should be restricted to what is known by opinion, not what is not known by it. That is because the statement of a Companion, if it is not known by opinion – i.e., by ijtihad – has the ruling of marfu', thus it is from the speech of the Lawgiver, and the concept in it is not considered. So what is meant by narrations is what is narrated in books from the mujtahids among the Companions and others. And in al-Nahr also under 'Sunnah of Wudu': The concepts of books are evidence unlike most concepts of texts. And in Ghayat al-Bayan under his statement: 'And the woman does not have to undo her braids,' he restricted by 'woman' as opposed to man. And specifying something in narrations indicates the negation of what is other than it by agreement, unlike texts, for in them it does not indicate negation of what is other than it according to us. And in Ghayat al-Bayan also: In the chapter of Hajj violations under his statement: 'And if a predator attacks a muhrim and he kills it, nothing is due on him'; because it is narrated that Umar killed a predator and offered a ram as a sacrifice, and said: 'We initiated it.' He reasoned his sacrifice by his own initiation, so it is known by this that if the muhrim did not initiate killing it but rather killed it to repel its attack, nothing is due on him; otherwise there would be no benefit in the reasoning. And it is not said: 'Specifying something by mention does not indicate negation of what is other than it according to you, so how do you infer from the statement of Umar?' Because we say: That is in the addresses of the Law, but in narrations and rational matters it does indicate, and Umar's reasoning is of the category of rational matters. The summary: That reasoning for rulings is sometimes by a legal text from a verse or hadith, and sometimes by reason as here, and rational causes are not from the speech of the Lawgiver, so their concept is considered. For this reason, you see them saying: 'The requirement of this cause is permissibility or prohibition of such-and-such,' and they infer by its concept. If you say: He said in al-Ashbah from the book of Judiciary: 'It is not permissible to argue by the concept in people's speech in the apparent school as evidence, while the concept of a narration is a proof, as in Ghayat al-Bayan from Hajj.' This contradicts what has passed that it is not considered only in the speech of the Lawgiver. I say: What the later scholars adopt is what we have presented. And Allama al-Bayri said in his commentary: And what is in al-Zahiriyya: 'Arguing by the concept is not permissible. That is the apparent school according to our scholars, and what he mentioned...'
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage addresses a key methodological rule in Hanafi usul al-ifta: the consideration of the legal concept (mafhum al-mukhalafa) in different contexts. The author begins by citing Shams al-A'imma al-Kardari (via Jalal al-Din al-Khazzazi) who makes a fundamental distinction: in the speech of the Lawgiver (khitabat al-shar'), specifying something by mention does not imply the negation of the ruling from everything else (i.e., mafhum al-mukhalafa is not valid). However, in people's everyday understanding, customs, transactions, and rational matters, such specification does imply negation. This view was adopted by the later Hanafi scholars (muta'akhkhirun) and is recorded in standard texts like Khizanat al-Akmal and al-Fatawa al-Khaniyya. An example is given: if someone says 'You do not owe me more than one hundred dirhams,' it is an acknowledgment of one hundred dirhams only—the concept excludes amounts above and below. (The phrase 'nor less' is added for emphasis; it does not create ambiguity.) The text then cites al-Nahr to refine the rule further: the concept is considered valid in narrations (riwayat) from mujtahid scholars (like the Companions) by agreement, but not in the texts of revelation (nusus). However, a Companion's statement that is not based on personal opinion (i.e., that could only be from revelation) is treated as marfu', i.e., as if from the Prophet, so the concept is not considered in such statements. In Ghayat al-Bayan, an example from Hajj shows how a ruling of Umar (killing a predator and sacrificing a ram) is reasoned: Umar explained his sacrifice by saying 'We initiated it' (i.e., we provoked the predator), so the concept indicates that if the muhrim does not initiate aggression, no sacrifice is due. This reasoning is rational (ma'qul), not from a sacred text, so its concept is valid. The author then addresses an apparent contradiction: al-Ashbah says that concept is not allowed in people's speech as evidence, while the same source elsewhere says concept of narrations is a proof. The resolution is that the later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) adopt the view that concept is valid in non-Shar'i contexts, and this is the relied-upon position (mufta bih). Finally, al-Allama al-Bayri notes that al-Zahiriyya records the opposite view—that arguing by concept is not permissible—as the apparent madhhab. This shows that there is some difference of opinion, but the later tradition favors one side.

Key Terms
المفهوم (al-mafhum): The inferred opposite meaning from a restricted expression (mafhum al-mukhalafa).
تخصيص الشيء بالذكر (takhsis al-shay' bi al-dhikr): Specifying something by mentioning it, implying that the ruling applies only to that thing.
خطابات الشارع (khitabat al-shari'): The direct speech of the Lawgiver (Allah and His Messenger) in revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rule presented, when is the consideration of mafhum (concept) not valid?
A) In the speech of the Lawgiver (Quran and hadith).
B) In people's customs and mutual understanding.
C) In transactions and rational matters.
D) In narrations from mujtahid Companions.

Key Takeaway
Mafhum al-mukhalafa is a valid indicator in all speech except the direct speech of the Lawgiver.

Two Hanafi Sayings on the Validity of Mafhum as Proof
Internal Hanafi dispute on mafhum as proof, with qa'idah and furuat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Hanafi positions on mafhum as a proof, apply the qa'idah of specification to fiqh cases, and determine the mufta bihi position for fatwa.

Core Idea
Mafhum is accepted in human speech, but in Shari' speech the apparent madhhab rejects it.

This passage from the commentary on 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' addresses a critical methodological question: can implied meaning (mafhum) serve as a proof in deriving rulings? Within the Hanafi school, there are two transmitted positions. Understanding the scope of mafhum is essential for a mufti, as it affects how one derives rulings from Qur'an, Hadith, and common speech.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
The passage states that the Hanafis have two sayings (qawlayn) regarding mafhum. One is the apparent madhhab (zahir al-riwaya) that mafhum is not a proof; the other, from Imam Muhammad in al-Siyar al-Kabir, accepts it.
The apparent madhhab is the well-known transmitted position of the early imams.
2
Examine the proofs
The proof for acceptance is the hadith of Ali regarding the Magians, where specification implies permissibility of others. The proof for rejection is the principle that specification does not negate what is not mentioned.
The hadith is cited by Imam Muhammad to permit marrying Christian women.
3
Trace the qa'idah
The passage cites a qa'idah: specification by mention indicates negation in common understanding. This is a dabt (restricting maxim) that governs human speech.
The qa'idah is applied in contexts where people naturally understand implications.
4
Apply the furuat
Two applications: the commander's announcement implying prohibition of other banners, and the Prophet's specification of Magians implying permissibility of marrying Christian women.
These show the practical effect of accepting mafhum.
5
Determine the fatwa hierarchy
Al-Birri states that practice is on Imam Muhammad's position, but limited to non-Shar'i speech; however, al-Siyar al-Kabir's authority suggests it can be used in Shar'i speech as well.
The mufta bihi is to accept mafhum in human speech and, according to some, in Lawgiver's speech.

محمد في "السير"الكبير" من جواز الاحتجاج بالمفهوم، فذلك خلاف ظاهر الرواية.
السرخس
قال في حواشي "الكشف" : رأيت في "الفوائد الظهيرية" في باب ما يكره في الصلاة: أن الاحتجاج بالمفهوم يجوز، ذكره شمس الأئمة في السير "الكبير"، وقال بنى محمد مسائل السير على الاحتجاج بالمفهوم، وإلى هذا مال الخصاف وبنى عليه مسائل الحيل. وفي "المصفى": التخصيص بالذكر لا يدل على نفي ما عداه، قلنا: التخصيص في الروايات وفي متفاهم الناس، وفي المعقولات يدل على نفي ما عداه. (من النكاح) وفي "خزانة الروايات": القيد في الرواية ينفي ما عداه. وفي "السراجية": أما في متفاهم الناس من الأخبارات، فإن تخصيص الشيء بالذكر يدل على نفي ما عداه كذا ذكره السرخسي. أقول: الظاهر أن العمل على ما في "السير"، كما اختاره الخصاف في الحيل، و لم نر من خالفه والله تعالى أعلم. انتهى كلام البيري. أي إن العمل على جواز الاحتجاج بالمفهوم، لكن لا مطلقا، بل في غير كلام الشارع كما علمت مما قررناه وإلا فالذي رأيته في "السير" "الكبير" جواز العمل به حتى في كلام الشارع، فإنه ذكر في باب آنية المشركين وذبائحهم أن تزوج نساء النصارى من أهل الحرب لا يحرم، واستدل عليه بحديث علي : " أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كتب إلى مجوس هجر رضي عند - يدعوهم إلى الإسلام فمن أسلم قبل منه، ومن لم يسلم ضربت عليه الجزية في أن لا يؤكل له ذبيحة، ولا ينكح منهم امرأة".

شرح عقود رسم المفتي
۷۳
للحنفية قولين في اعتبار المفهوم
قال شمس الأئمة السرخسي في شرحه: "فكأنه أي محمدا استدل بتخصيص رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم المجوس بذلك، على أنه لا بأس بنكاح نساء أهل الكتاب، فإنه بنى هذا الكتاب على أن المفهوم حجة، ويأتي بيان ذلك في موضعه .
ثم قال بعد أربعة أبواب في باب ما يجب من طاعة الوالي في قول محمد: لو قال منادي الأمير: من أراد العلف فليخرج تحت لواء "فلان" فهذا بمنزلة النهي، أي نهيهم عن أن يفارقوا صاحب اللواء بعد خروجهم معه، وقد بينا أنه بنى هذا الكتاب على أن المفهوم حجة وظاهر المذهب عندنا أن المفهوم ليس بحجة، مفهوم الصفة ومفهوم الشرط في ذلك سواء، ولكنه اعتبر المقصود الذي يفهمه أكثر الناس في هذا الموضوع؛ لأن الغزاة في الغالب لا يقفون على حقائق العلوم، وأن أميرهم هذا اللفظ إنما نهى الناس عن الخروج إلا تحت لواء فلان، فجعل النهي المعلوم بدلالة كلامه كالمنصوص عليه". ومقتضاه أن ظاهر المذهب أن المفهوم ليس بحجة حتى في كلام الناس؛ لأن ما ذكره في هذا الباب من كلام الأمير، فهو من كلام الناس، لا من كلام الشارع. وهذا موافق لما مر عن "الأشباه". والظاهر أن القول بكونه حجة في كلامهم قول المتأخرين كما يعلم من عبارة "شرح التحرير" السابقة. ولعل مستندهم في ذلك ما نقلناه آنفا عن السير الكبير"، فإنه من كتب ظاهر الرواية الستة، بل هو آخرها تصنيفا، فالعمل عليه كما قدمناه في النظم.
For the Hanafis there are two sayings regarding considering the implied meaning (mafhum). Commentary on the Contract of the Mufti's Diagram. 72. Muhammad in 'al-Siyar al-Kabir' permitted argumentation by implied meaning, so that is contrary to the apparent narration. Al-Sarakhsi said in the glosses of 'al-Kashf': I saw in 'al-Fawa'id al-Zahirah' in the chapter on what is disliked in prayer: that argumentation by implied meaning is permissible; Shams al-A'immah mentioned it in 'al-Siyar al-Kabir', and he said: Muhammad built the issues of al-Siyar on argumentation by implied meaning, and al-Khassaf inclined to this and built on it the issues of legal stratagems. And in 'al-Musaffa': specification by mention does not indicate the negation of what is besides it. We say: specification in narrations and in common understanding among people, and in rational matters, indicates the negation of what is besides it. (From marriage) And in 'Khizanat al-Riwayat': the restriction in a narration negates what is besides it. And in 'al-Sirajiyyah': as for narrations in common understanding among people, specification of a thing by mention indicates the negation of what is besides it; thus al-Sarakhsi mentioned it. I say: The apparent is that the practice is upon what is in 'al-Siyar', as al-Khassaf chose in legal stratagems, and we have not seen anyone opposing him; and Allah knows best. End of al-Birri's speech. That is, practice is upon the permissibility of argumentation by implied meaning, but not absolutely; rather, in other than the speech of the Lawgiver, as you have learned from what we established. Otherwise, what I have seen in 'al-Siyar al-Kabir' is the permissibility of acting upon it even in the speech of the Lawgiver. For he mentioned in the chapter of the vessels of the polytheists and their slaughtered animals that marrying Christian women from the people of war is not forbidden, and he used as evidence the hadith of 'Ali: 'The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, wrote to the Magians of Hajar... inviting them to Islam; whoever accepted Islam was accepted from him, and whoever did not accept Islam, jizya was imposed on him; that no slaughtered animal of his may be eaten, nor may a woman of them be married.' Commentary on the Contract of the Mufti's Diagram. 73. For the Hanafis there are two sayings regarding considering the implied meaning. Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi said in his commentary: 'It is as if he, meaning Muhammad, used as evidence the specification of the Messenger of Allah, upon him be peace, of the Magians by that, to show that there is no harm in marrying women of the People of the Book. For he built this book on the principle that implied meaning is a proof, and its clarification will come in its place.' Then he said after four chapters in the chapter on the necessity of obeying the ruler: In Muhammad's statement: 'If the crier of the commander says: Whoever wants fodder, let him go out under the banner of so-and-so'—this is tantamount to a prohibition, i.e., a prohibition for them to separate from the owner of the banner after going out with him. And we have explained that he built this book on the principle that implied meaning is a proof, while the apparent school of thought with us is that implied meaning is not a proof, the concept of description and the concept of condition being equal in that. But he considered the intended meaning that most people understand in this context, because the fighters generally are not acquainted with the realities of knowledge, and that their commander only used this phrase to prohibit people from going out except under the banner of so-and-so, thus he made the prohibition known by the indication of his speech like the explicit text.' And its import is that the apparent school of thought is that implied meaning is not a proof even in the speech of people, because what he mentioned in this chapter about the speech of the commander is the speech of people, not the speech of the Lawgiver. This is consistent with what was mentioned from 'al-Ashbah'. And the apparent is that the saying that it is a proof in their speech is the saying of the later scholars, as known from the previous phrase of 'Sharh al-Tahrir'. And perhaps their basis for that is what we quoted earlier from 'al-Siyar al-Kabir', for it is among the six books of the apparent narration; indeed it is the last of them in authorship, so practice is upon it as we have presented in the versification.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' addresses a critical methodological question in Hanafi usul al-iftā: whether implied meaning (mafhum) can serve as a proof (hujja). It opens by stating that the Hanafis have two positions on this issue. The first position, attributed to Imam Muhammad in his 'al-Siyar al-Kabir', permits argumentation by mafhum, contrary to the well-known apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya). Al-Sarakhsi notes in his glosses that even in the chapter on what is disliked in prayer, mafhum is accepted. Imam Muhammad built many rulings in al-Siyar on mafhum, and al-Khassaf followed this in his work on legal stratagems (al-Hiyal). The opposing view holds that specification by mention does not negate what is not mentioned. The commentator al-Birri then clarifies that the relied-upon view is to practice on Imam Muhammad's position, but not absolutely: mafhum is a proof in human speech (e.g., commands of a commander) but not in the speech of the Lawgiver (Shar'i). However, he notes that in al-Siyar al-Kabir, Imam Muhammad even used mafhum in interpreting the Lawgiver's speech, as in the hadith about the Magians of Hajar. Al-Sarakhsi explains that Imam Muhammad's use of mafhum in the context of the commander's announcement is based on common understanding, not on a general principle, because the soldiers understand the implied prohibition. The passage concludes that the later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) adopted the view that mafhum is a proof in human speech, possibly relying on al-Siyar al-Kabir, which is one of the six books of Zahir al-Riwaya and the last authored, so it carries weight. This shows that within the Hanafi school, there is a spectrum of acceptance of mafhum, depending on the context and the authority of the source.

Key Terms
المفهوم (al-mafhum): The implied meaning or understanding derived from a specified expression, opposite of mantuq (explicit statement).
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The well-known transmitted position of the early Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani) recorded in the six major books.
السير الكبير (al-Siyar al-Kabir): A major work by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani on Islamic international law, considered one of the six books of Zahir al-Riwaya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for Imam Muhammad's acceptance of mafhum in al-Siyar al-Kabir?
A) The hadith of Ali about Magians
B) The principle that specification negates what is not mentioned in common understanding
C) Both A and B
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two positions on mafhum: the apparent madhhab rejects it, but the relied-upon practice accepts it in human speech, and even in Shari' speech due to the authority of al-Siyar al-Kabir.

The Authority of Mafhum in Hanafi Fatwa: Two Opinions and the Relied-upon View
Exposition of Hanafi ikhtilaf on mafhum and the confirmed operative view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Hanafi positions on mafhum and apply the confirmed view (mufta bihi) that mafhum is authoritative in non-divine speech.

Core Idea
Mafhum is not a proof in divine speech, but it is authoritative in people's speech — a critical distinction for fatwa.

The passage introduces an important methodological rule for the mufti: whether implied meanings (mafhum) can be used as legal evidence. While the early school rejected mafhum entirely, Imam Muhammad's practice in al-Siyar al-Kabir and the later scholars' consensus have established a nuanced position that distinguishes between divine and human speech. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly deriving rulings from non-Shar'i statements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opinions
State the two positions on mafhum within the Hanafi school: (1) the apparent position (zahir al-madhhab) that mafhum is not a proof (laysa bi hujjah), and (2) the later view that mafhum is authoritative in non-divine speech.
The first view applies to all speech; the second limits the rejection to divine speech.
2
Analyze Imam Muhammad's usage
See how Imam Muhammad employed mafhum in al-Siyar al-Kabir to derive a ruling from the Prophet's specific mention of Magians, inferring permission to marry People of the Book.
He treated the implied meaning as explicit because of the context of soldiers who understand implications.
3
Distinguish the basis
Understand why the later scholars considered this an exception: Imam Muhammad's usage was based on 'urf (custom) and the common understanding of people, not on a general acceptance of mafhum as a proof.
The exception applies only to non-divine speech (kalam al-nas).
4
Apply the rule
Determine when mafhum can be used in fatwa according to the confirmed view: the mufti may rely on mafhum from people's statements (e.g., contracts, conditions) but not from the Quran or Sunnah.
This distinction is critical for deriving rulings from everyday language.
5
Evaluate the authority
Recognize that the later view is based on a Zahir al-Riwayah text (al-Siyar al-Kabir) and is the operative position (al-‘amal ‘alayh) for fatwa.
Despite being a late refinement, it carries the weight of the core transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
للحنفية قولين في اعتبار المفهوم
قال شمس الأئمة السرخسي في شرحه: "فكأنه أي محمدا استدل بتخصيص رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم المجوس بذلك، على أنه لا بأس بنكاح نساء أهل الكتاب، فإنه بنى هذا الكتاب على أن المفهوم حجة، ويأتي بيان ذلك في موضعه .
ثم قال بعد أربعة أبواب في باب ما يجب من طاعة الوالي في قول محمد: لو قال منادي الأمير: من أراد العلف فليخرج تحت لواء "فلان" فهذا بمنزلة النهي، أي نهيهم عن أن يفارقوا صاحب اللواء بعد خروجهم معه، وقد بينا أنه بنى هذا الكتاب على أن المفهوم حجة وظاهر المذهب عندنا أن المفهوم ليس بحجة، مفهوم الصفة ومفهوم الشرط في ذلك سواء، ولكنه اعتبر المقصود الذي يفهمه أكثر الناس في هذا الموضوع؛ لأن الغزاة في الغالب لا يقفون على حقائق العلوم، وأن أميرهم هذا اللفظ إنما نهى الناس عن الخروج إلا تحت لواء فلان، فجعل النهي المعلوم بدلالة كلامه كالمنصوص عليه". ومقتضاه أن ظاهر المذهب أن المفهوم ليس بحجة حتى في كلام الناس؛ لأن ما ذكره في هذا الباب من كلام الأمير، فهو من كلام الناس، لا من كلام الشارع. وهذا موافق لما مر عن "الأشباه". والظاهر أن القول بكونه حجة في كلامهم قول المتأخرين كما يعلم من عبارة "شرح التحرير" السابقة. ولعل مستندهم في ذلك ما نقلناه آنفا عن "السير الكبير"، فإنه من كتب ظاهر الرواية الستة، بل هو آخرها تصنيفا، فالعمل عليه كما قدمناه في النظم.
The Hanafis have two opinions regarding considering the implied meaning (mafhum). Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said in his commentary: "It is as if Muhammad used the specific reference of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) to the Magians to deduce that there is no harm in marrying women of the People of the Book, because he built this book on the premise that the implied meaning is authoritative, and its explanation will come in its place." Then he said after four chapters in the chapter on the duty of obeying the ruler in Muhammad's statement: "If the commander's herald says: 'Whoever wants fodder should go out under the banner of so-and-so,' this is like a prohibition, i.e., prohibiting them from leaving the banner's leader after going out with him. We have explained that he built this book on the premise that the implied meaning is authoritative, while the apparent position in our school is that the implied meaning is not authoritative—the implied meaning of description and the implied meaning of condition are the same in that regard. But he considered the intended meaning that most people understand in this context, because warriors generally do not grasp the realities of knowledge, and that their commander's word actually prohibited people from going out except under the banner of so-and-so, so he made the prohibition known by implication of his speech like the explicit text." The implication is that the apparent school position is that the implied meaning is not authoritative even in people's speech, because what he mentioned in this chapter from the commander's speech is from people's speech, not from the speech of the Lawgiver. This agrees with what was mentioned in al-Ashbah. It appears that the opinion that it is authoritative in their speech is the opinion of the later scholars, as understood from the previous expression of Sharh al-Tahrir. Perhaps their basis is what we quoted earlier from al-Siyar al-Kabir, for it is among the six books of manifest transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah), indeed it is the last of them in composition, so action is upon it as we have presented in the versification.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage addresses a methodological rule for the mufti: the authority of implied meanings (mafhum) in the Hanafi school. It begins by noting there are two opinions among Hanafis on whether mafhum is a valid proof. The text quotes Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi's commentary on al-Siyar al-Kabir, where he explains that Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (in al-Siyar al-Kabir) treated mafhum as authoritative, deducing from the Prophet's specific mention of Magians that marrying women of the People of the Book is permissible. However, Sarakhsi clarifies that the apparent position (zahir al-madhhab) of the Hanafi school is that mafhum is not a proof—whether it is mafhum al-sifah (implication of description) or mafhum al-shart (implication of condition). Imam Muhammad's usage in al-Siyar al-Kabir is an exception based on the common understanding of people in that military context; he treated the implied prohibition as explicit because soldiers are not jurists. The passage concludes that the later Hanafi scholars (mutakhkhirin) have adopted the view that mafhum is authoritative in non-divine speech, relying on Imam Muhammad's practice in al-Siyar al-Kabir, which is part of the six core books of Zahir al-Riwayah. This is the relied-upon position (al-‘amal ‘alayh) for issuing fatwas.

Key Terms
المفهوم (al-mafhum): The implied or understood meaning derived from the wording of a text, as opposed to the explicit statement (al-mantuq).
ظاهر المذهب (zahir al-madhhab): The apparent or most well-known position of the Hanafi school, as transmitted by the early masters (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad).
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The six core books authored by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that contain the authoritative rulings of the early Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the apparent school position (zahir al-madhhab) of the Hanafis regarding mafhum?
A) Mafhum is always a valid proof.
B) Mafhum is not a valid proof.
C) Mafhum is valid only in divine speech.
D) Mafhum is valid only in conditions.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufti relies on mafhum in human speech but not in divine speech — a critical distinction for proper fatwa.

Consideration of Mafhum and Priority of Explicit Text
Explains when mafhum is authoritative and that explicit text takes precedence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain when mafhum is authoritative in Hanafi usul and identify the condition that explicit text overrides mafhum.

Core Idea
Mafhum is considered in non-Shar'i speech but yields to explicit text; Quranic restrictions may be coincidental.

This passage from a rasm al-mufti text addresses a key distinction: the implied meaning (mafhum) of a statement is treated differently depending on the speaker. In the speech of the Lawgiver, rhetorical nuance often means restrictions are not always intended as conditions. In people's speech, however, we assume restrictions are deliberate. The passage also introduces the crucial rule that if an explicit text (sarih) exists, it overrides any implied meaning. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for a mufti when weighing evidence.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two contexts of speech
Identify that mafhum is authoritative in non-Shar'i speech (kalam al-nas) but not automatically in Shar'i speech due to eloquence.
The Quranic example establishes that restrictions may be descriptive, not prescriptive.
2
Analyze the Quranic example
Examine verse 4:23 'wa raba'ibukum allati fi hujurikum'. The restriction 'fi hujurikum' is dominant (aghlabi), not a condition.
3
Understand the role of custom
Recognize that custom (urf) establishes implied meanings as if they were explicit, following the maxim 'al-ma'ruf ka al-mashrut'.
This applies to people's speech and scholarly works.
4
Apply to narrations and fiqh works
Scholars routinely use conditions to signal exclusion; this is a dominant practice (aghlabi) but not absolute.
Counterexample from al-Hidayah: washing hands upon waking is coincidental, not an intentional condition.
5
Apply the overriding rule
If an explicit text (sarih) exists, it takes precedence over any mafhum. The mafhum is only considered when no sarih contradicts it.
This is a fundamental principle in ranking evidences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
توجيه اعتبار المفهوم وعدم اعتباره ]

والحاصل أن العمل الآن على اعتبار المفهوم في غير كلام الشارع؛ لأن التنصيص على الشيء في كلامه لا يلزم منه أن يكون فائدته النفي عما عداه؛ لأن كلامه معدن ،البلاغة، فقد يكون مراده غير ذلك، كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَرَبَائِبُكُمُ اللَّاتِي فِي حُجُورِكُمْ (النساء: ٢٣)؛ فإن فائدة التقييد بالحجور كون ذلك هو الغالب في الربائب. وأما كلام الناس فهو خالٍ عن هذه المزية، فيستدل بكلامهم على المفهوم؛ لأنه المتعارف بينهم.
وقد صرح في "شرح السير الكبير بأن الثابت بالعرف كالثابت بالنص، وهو قريب من قول الفقهاء: "المعروف كالمشروط" وحينئذ فما ثبت بالعرف فكأن قائله نص عليه، فيعمل به.
وكذا يقال في مفهوم الروايات؛ فإن العلماء جرت عادتهم في كتبهم على أنهم يذكرون القيود والشروط ونحوها، تنبيهاً على إخراج ما ليس فيه ذلك القيد ونحوه، وأن حكمه مخالف لحكم المنطوق، وهذا مما شاع وذاع بينهم بلا نكير، ولذا لم يُرَ من صرّح بخلافه. نعم ذلك أغلبي كما عزاه القهستاني في "شرح النقاية" إلى حدود "النهاية". ومن غير الغالب قول الهداية : وسنن الطهارة: غسل اليدين قبل إدخالهما الإناء، إذا استيقظ المتوضئ من نومه"؛ فإن التقييد بالاستيقاظ اتفاقي، وقع تبركاً بلفظ الحديث، فإن السنة تشمل المستيقظ وغيره عند الأكثرين. وقيل: إنه احترازي؛ لإخراج غير المستيقظ، وإليه مال شمس الأئمة الكردري.
وقولي: "ما لم يخالف لصريح ثبتا أي إن المفهوم حجة على ما قررناه إذا لم يخالف صريحا، فإن الصريح مقدّم على المفهوم، كما صرح به الطرسوسي وغيره، وذكره الأصوليون في ترجيح الأدلة، فإن القائلين باعتبار المفهوم في الأدلة الشرعية إنما يعتبرونه إذا لم يأت صريح بخلافه، فيقدّم الصريح، ويلغى المفهوم. والله تعالى أعلم.
The explanation: Consideration of the implied meaning (mafhum) and non-consideration thereof. The conclusion is that practice now is on considering the implied meaning in other than the speech of the Lawgiver; because specifying something in His speech does not necessarily entail that its benefit is negation of what is besides it; because His speech is a mine of eloquence, so His intention may be otherwise, as in His statement: {and your step-daughters who are in your guardianship} (an-Nisa 23); for the benefit of restricting to guardianship is that this is predominant regarding step-daughters. As for people's speech, it is free from this excellence, so one infers from their speech the implied meaning because that is what is customary among them. And it is explicitly stated in 'Sharh al-Siyar al-Kabir' that what is established by custom is like what is established by text, and it is close to the jurists' statement: 'The known is like the stipulated'. Therefore, what is established by custom is as if the speaker explicitly stated it, so it is acted upon. Likewise, it is said regarding the implied meaning of narrations; for scholars have an established practice in their books that they mention restrictions, conditions, and the like, as a warning to exclude what does not have that restriction or similar, and that its ruling is contrary to the ruling of the explicit statement. This has become widespread and publicized among them without objection, and thus no one has been seen who explicitly opposed it. Yes, this is on a dominant basis, as al-Qahistani attributed in 'Sharh al-Niqaya' to the limits of 'al-Nihaya'. And from the non-dominant is the statement of al-Hidayah: 'The sunan of purification: washing the hands before inserting them into the vessel when the one performing wudu awakens from his sleep'; for the restriction to awakening is coincidental, occurring as a blessing of the wording of the hadith, for the sunna includes the awakened and others according to the majority. And it is said that it is intentionally restrictive to exclude the non-awakened, and that is what Shams al-A'imma al-Kardari inclined to. And my statement: 'As long as it does not contradict an explicit text that is established' i.e., the implied meaning is proof according to what we have established, provided it does not contradict an explicit text, for the explicit takes precedence over the implied, as stated by al-Tarsusi and others, and mentioned by usuliyyun in the ranking of evidences. Indeed, those who consider the implied meaning in legal evidence only consider it if no explicit statement to the contrary comes, then the explicit is given precedence and the implied is disregarded. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage addresses a key rasm al-mufti principle: the weight of mafhum (implied meaning) in different contexts. The author begins by stating the current practice: mafhum is considered authoritative only in non-Shar'i speech (kalam al-nas). This is because the Lawgiver's speech (kalam al-Shari') is filled with rhetorical nuance; a restriction may be mentioned for a reason other than negating what is not mentioned. The example from Quran 4:23 is given: the phrase 'fi hujurikum' (in your guardianship) is a common occurrence (ghalib), not a condition for ruling. In people's speech, however, such nuance is absent, so we take their restrictions as intentional. The passage then connects this to custom (urf): what is established by custom is like a textual stipulation. The same applies to the mafhum of narrations in fiqh books; scholars routinely mention conditions to signal that the omitted cases have a different ruling. However, this is probabilistic (aghlabi), not absolute. A counterexample from al-Hidayah is discussed: the sunan of washing hands upon waking is restricted to the awakened, but most hold this is coincidental (ittifaqi) due to the hadith wording, not an intentional exclusion. Finally, the author clarifies his own condition: mafhum is only proof if it does not contradict an explicit text (sarih). If a clear textual statement exists, it takes precedence and the mafhum is ignored. This is a fundamental rule in ranking evidences.

Key Terms
مفهوم (mafhum): The implied meaning or converse of a statement: what is understood from the wording that the ruling applies only to the mentioned case, excluding others.
منطوق (mantuq): The explicit statement: what is directly expressed by the wording.
صريح (sarih): An explicit text that is clear and unambiguous, taking precedence over implied meanings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for mafhum to be considered authoritative?
A) It must be from the Quran or Sunnah.
B) It must not contradict an explicit text (sarih).
C) It must be supported by consensus.
D) It must be from the speech of scholars.

Key Takeaway
Mafhum is a valid legal indicator in non-Shar'i contexts, but it always yields to an explicit text, and its use in divine speech is limited due to rhetorical nuance.

15 min
The Mufti's Consideration of Custom
Rules for mufti to consider custom and people's conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the role of custom (urf) in Hanafi fatwa and apply the principle that a mufti may prefer a weaker madhhab position if custom and public interest demand it, while staying within shariah limits.

Core Idea
A mufti must weigh custom; he may depart from the apparent madhhab if custom changes and no shariah violation occurs.

In this passage, we learn that a mufti is not a mere transmitter of texts. He must be attuned to the people's customs and conditions. The author draws on Hanafi authorities to show that custom can override the apparent madhhab, provided it does not contradict the clear injunctions of Shariah. This lesson will train you to recognise when and how to apply this critical rasm al-mufti rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core principle
Recognize that custom (urf) is a valid basis for fatwa, and the mufti must know it. The passage opens with 'اعتبار للعرف الحادث' (consideration is given to the arising custom).
2
Assess the mufti's qualifications
The mufti needs sound opinion, knowledge of shariah principles, and training under an expert. Even memorising all books is insufficient without apprenticeship.
Refer to the quote from Munyat al-Mufti.
3
Apply the custom rule to examples
Analyse the Qasamah and fasting cases where the mufti chooses between different opinions based on custom, harm, and the person's condition.
Qasamah: Abu Hanifa's view rejected; Sahibayn accepted. Fasting: choose between Abu Yusuf and Zufar based on the person's nature.
4
Recognise the limits
Custom is followed only as long as it does not contradict Shariah. Examples of prohibited customs include illegal tolls (al-maks) and usury (al-riba).
Final part of the passage: 'ما لم يخالف الشريعة'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاعتبار للعرف الحادث كان في عرف زمانه، وتغيّر عرفه إلى عرف آخر، اقتداء بهم. لكن بعد أن يكون المفتي ممن له رأي ونظر صحيح، ومعرفة بقواعد الشرع حتى يميز بين العرف الذي يجوز بناء الأحكام عليه وبين غيره؛ فإن المتقدمين شرطوا في المفتي الاجتهاد وهذا مفقود في زماننا، فلا أقل أن يشترط فيه معرفة المسائل بشروطها وقيودها التي كثيرا ما يسقطونها، ولا يصرحون بها اعتمادا على فهم المتفقه. وكذا لا بد له من معرفة عرف زمانه وأحوال أهله، والتخرج في ذلك على أستاذ ماهر، ولذا قال في آخر "منية المفتي": لو أن الرجل حفظ جميع كتب أصحابنا لا بد أن يتلمذ للفتوى، حتى يهتدي إليه؛ لأن كثيرا من المسائل يجاب عنه على عادات أهل الزمان فيما لا يخالف الشريعة. وفي "القنية": ليس للمفتي ولا للقاضي أن يحكما على ظاهر المذهب ويتركا العرف ونقله منها في "خزانة الروايات". وهذا صريح فيما قلنا المفتي لا يفتي بخلاف عرف أهل زمانه. ويقرب منه ما نقله في "الأشباه" عن "البزازية" من أن المفتي يفتي بما يقع عنده من وكتبت في "ردّ المحتار" في باب القسامة فيما لو ادعى الولي على رجل من غير أهل المحلّة، وشهد اثنان منهم عليه، لم تقبل عنده، وقالا: تقبل إلخ. نقل السيد الحموي عن العلامة المقدسي أنه قال: توقفت عن الفتوى بقول الإمام، ومنعت من إشاعته؛ لما يترتب عليه من الضرر العام، فإن من عرفه من المتمردين يتجاسر على قتل النفس في المحلات الخالية من أهلها، معتمداً على عدم قبول شهادتهم عليه حتى قلت: ينبغي الفتوى على قولهما، لا سيّما والأحكام تختلف باختلاف الأيام. غير العرف إذا خالف الشريعة وقال في "فتح القدير" في باب ما يوجب القضاء والكفارة، من كتاب الصوم عند قول "الهداية": "ولو أكل لحماً بين أسنانه لم يفطر، وإن كان كثيراً يفطر، وقال زفر يفطر في الوجهين". ما نصه: "والتحقيق أن المفتي في الوقائع لا بد له من ضرب اجتهاد ومعرفة بأحوال الناس، وقد عرف أن الكفارة تفتقر إلى كمال الجناية، فينظر إلى صاحب الواقعة إن كان ممن يعاف طبعه ذلك أخذ بقول أبي يوسف، وإن كان ممن لا أثر لذلك عنده، أخذ بقول زفر". وفي "تصحيح العلامة قاسم" فإن قلت: قد يحكون أقوالاً من غير ترجيح، وقد يختلفون في التصحيح؟ قلت يعمل بمثل ما علموا من اعتبار تغير العرف، وأحوال الناس، وما هو الأرفق بالناس، وما ظهر عليه التعامل، وما قوي وجهه، ولا يخلو الوجود من تمييز هذا حقيقةً لا ظناً بنفسه، ويرجع من لم يميز إلى من يميّز لبراءة ذمته. فهذا كله صريح فيما قلنا من العمل بالعرف ما لم يخالف الشريعة، كالمكس والربا ونحو ذلك. فلا بد للمفتي والقاضي بل والمجتهد من معرفة أحوال الناس، وقد قالوا ومن جهل بأهل زمانه فهو جاهل. وقدّمنا أنهم قالوا: يفتي بقول أبي يوسف فيما يتعلق بالقضاء؛ لكونه جرّب الوقائع، وعرف أحوال الناس. وفي البحر عن "مناقب الإمام محمد" للكردري كان محمد يذهب إلى الصباغين، ويسأل عن معاملتهم، وما يديرونها فيما بينهم.
Consideration is given to the custom that arises in the custom of his time, and if his custom changes to another custom, following them. But only after the mufti is one who has sound opinion and insight, and knowledge of the principles of Shariah so that he can distinguish between the custom upon which rulings may be based and other customs. For the early scholars stipulated ijtihad in the mufti, and this is lacking in our time. So the least that can be required of him is knowledge of the issues with their conditions and restrictions, which they often omit and do not mention explicitly, relying on the understanding of the student of fiqh. Likewise, he must know the custom of his time and the conditions of its people, and be trained in that under a skilled teacher. Hence it is said in the end of 'Munyat al-Mufti': If a man memorizes all the books of our companions, he must still apprentice for fatwa until he is guided to it; because many issues are answered according to the customs of the people of the time, as long as they do not contradict Shariah. In 'al-Qunyah': It is not permissible for the mufti or the judge to rule according to the apparent madhhab and leave aside custom, and it is quoted from 'Khanat al-Riwayat'. This is explicit in what we said: the mufti does not issue fatwa contrary to the custom of the people of his time. Close to this is what is quoted in 'al-Ashbah' from 'al-Bazzaziyyah' that the mufti issues fatwa according to what occurs to him. And I wrote in 'Radd al-Muhtar' in the chapter of Qasamah regarding a case where the heir accuses a man not from the inhabitants of the locality, and two of them testify against him, according to him (Abu Hanifa) it is not accepted, but they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said it is accepted, etc. Al-Sayyid al-Hamawi narrated from al-Allamah al-Maqdisi that he said: I hesitated to give fatwa according to the statement of the Imam, and I prevented its propagation because of the general harm that would result. For those who know it from the rebellious ones become bold to kill a person in localities devoid of their inhabitants, relying on the non-acceptance of their testimony against him, until I said: It is appropriate to give fatwa according to their statement (the two), especially since rulings vary with the variation of times. Otherwise, custom when it contradicts Shariah. And he said in 'Fath al-Qadir' in the chapter of what necessitates qada' and kaffarah from the book of fasting, at the statement of 'al-Hidayah': 'If one eats meat stuck between his teeth, he does not break fast, but if it is a lot he breaks fast; Zufar said he breaks fast in both cases.' Its text: 'The investigation is that the mufti in incidents must have a degree of ijtihad and knowledge of the conditions of people. It is known that kaffarah requires complete violation. So he looks at the person of the incident: if he is one whose nature abhors that, he takes the statement of Abu Yusuf, and if he is one for whom that has no effect, he takes the statement of Zufar.' In 'Tashih al-Allamah Qasim', if you say: They often narrate statements without preference, and they differ in tashih? I say: He acts according to what they know of considering change of custom, the conditions of people, what is more convenient for people, what has become the practice, and what has strong support. Existence is not free from distinguishing this in reality, not merely in opinion, by oneself. And whoever cannot distinguish returns to one who can, to discharge his responsibility. All this is explicit in what we said: acting by custom as long as it does not contradict Shariah, like illegal tolls, usury, and the like. So the mufti, the judge, and even the mujtahid must know the conditions of people. They said: Whoever is ignorant of the people of his time is ignorant. We have already mentioned that they said: He gives fatwa according to the statement of Abu Yusuf in matters related to judiciary, because he experienced incidents and knew the conditions of people. In 'al-Bahr' from 'Manaqib al-Imam Muhammad' by al-Kardari: Muhammad would go to the dyers and ask about their transactions and what they conduct among themselves.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule (rasm al-mufti) concerning the mufti's consideration of custom (urf) when issuing fatwas. It opens by affirming that custom is given weight, especially when custom changes over time. However, this is conditional: the mufti must possess sound judgment, knowledge of Shariah principles, and the ability to distinguish between valid custom and invalid one. Since the early scholars required ijtihad—now absent—the minimum is thorough knowledge of the issues with their conditions and restrictions. The mufti must also know the custom of his time and be trained under a skilled teacher. The text then quotes 'Munyat al-Mufti' emphasizing that even memorizing all books is insufficient; apprenticeship is needed because many answers depend on current customs. From 'al-Qunyah', it is clear that a mufti or judge should not rule by the apparent madhhab while ignoring custom. The 'Ashbah' and 'al-Bazzaziyyah' are cited to show that mufti follows what occurs to him. A case from 'Radd al-Muhtar' on qasamah illustrates: the mufti hesitated to follow Imam Abu Hanifa's stricter ruling because it would cause harm, advising to follow the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) whose ruling accepted the witnesses, thus preventing social harm. The text then references 'Fath al-Qadir' on fasting: for a slight impurity from meat between teeth, the mufti may choose Abu Yusuf's or Zufar's ruling based on the person's nature, showing flexibility. The need to consider change of custom, people's welfare, and common practice is stressed. The passage concludes emphatically: custom is followed as long as it doesn't contradict Shariah, and a mufti ignorant of his time's people is himself ignorant. The example of Imam Muhammad visiting dyers to learn their transactions underscores the necessity of being acquainted with people's dealings.

Key Terms
العرف (al-urf): Custom or prevailing practice of the people of a particular time and place, which can be the basis for fatwa as long as it does not contradict shariah.
المفتي (al-mufti): The jurist qualified to issue fatwas; here, one who must know custom and conditions of people, and may follow a weaker position in the madhhab due to changing custom or public interest.
ظاهر المذهب (zahir al-madhhab): The apparent or well-known position of the Hanafi madhhab, which may be set aside if custom contradicts it, provided it does not violate shariah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the minimum requirement for a mufti in the absence of ijtihad?
A) He must memorize all six books of Zahir al-Riwayah.
B) He must know the issues with their conditions and restrictions.
C) He must follow only the statements of Abu Hanifa.
D) He must apprentice under a judge for ten years.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must consider custom and may follow it over the apparent madhhab to prevent harm, as long as Shariah is not violated.

The Mufti's Consideration of Custom (al-Urf)
Explains the mufti's duty to consider custom and people's conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'Custom is considered as long as it does not contradict Shariah' to a mufti's fatwa by analyzing a person's condition and choosing the appropriate scholarly opinion.

Core Idea
Custom is valid unless it contradicts Shariah; the mufti must know people's conditions to give correct fatwa.

This passage from a commentary on Rasm al-Mufti teaches that a mufti cannot rely solely on transmitted rulings. He must exercise ijtihad and understand the customs and conditions of the people he serves. The maxim 'al-urf mu'tabar ma lam yukhalif al-shariah' guides him in choosing between differing opinions within the Hanafi school, as illustrated by the case of eating meat stuck between teeth while fasting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its scope
The primary tool is the principle that custom is legal evidence as long as it doesn't contradict Shariah. This applies across all chapters of fiqh.
The maxim is 'al-urf mu'tabar ma lam yukhalif al-shariah'.
2
Analyze the specific case
Meat stuck between teeth while fasting – note the dispute between Abu Yusuf (no kaffarah unless large) and Zufar (kaffarah always). The mufti must decide which opinion to follow.
The case is from the chapter on fasting in al-Hidayah.
3
Determine the mufti's role
The mufti must assess the individual's nature and custom. If the person's nature is repulsed by the meat, follow Abu Yusuf; otherwise, follow Zufar.
This involves ijtihad and knowledge of people's conditions.
4
Apply the maxim to the case
Apply the maxim: the mufti's decision is based on the person's custom (nature). This ensures the fatwa aligns with both Shariah and the individual's reality.
The maxim is not absolute; it is restricted by Shariah.
5
Generalize the methodology
The mufti must investigate actual customs (like Imam Muhammad visiting dyers) and prefer opinions of those who knew people's conditions (like Abu Yusuf in judicial matters).
Ignorance of people's conditions is ignorance itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العرف إذا خالف الشريعة وقال في "فتح القدير" في باب ما يوجب القضاء والكفارة، من كتاب الصوم عند قول "الهداية": "ولو أكل لحماً بين أسنانه لم يفطر، وإن كان كثيراً يفطر، وقال زفر يفطر في الوجهين". ما نصه: "والتحقيق أن المفتي في الوقائع لا بد له من ضرب اجتهاد ومعرفة بأحوال الناس، وقد عرف أن الكفارة تفتقر إلى كمال الجناية، فينظر إلى صاحب الواقعة إن كان ممن يعاف طبعه ذلك أخذ بقول أبي يوسف، وإن كان ممن لا أثر لذلك عنده، أخذ بقول زفر". وفي "تصحيح العلامة قاسم فإن قلت: قد يحكون أقوالاً من غير ترجيح، وقد يختلفون في التصحيح؟ قلت يعمل بمثل ما علموا من اعتبار تغير العرف، وأحوال الناس، وما هو الأرفق بالناس، وما ظهر عليه التعامل، وما قوي وجهه، ولا يخلو الوجود من تمييز هذا حقيقةً لا ظناً بنفسه، ويرجع من لم يميز إلى من يميّز لبراءة ذمته. فهذا كله صريح فيما قلنا من العمل بالعرف ما لم يخالف الشريعة، كالمكس والربا ونحو ذلك. فلا بد للمفتي والقاضي بل والمجتهد من معرفة أحوال الناس، وقد قالوا ومن جهل بأهل زمانه فهو جاهل. وقدّمنا أنهم قالوا: يفتي بقول أبي يوسف فيما يتعلق بالقضاء؛ لكونه جرّب الوقائع، وعرف أحوال الناس. وفي البحر" عن "مناقب الإمام محمد" للكردري كان محمد يذهب إلى الصباغين، ويسأل عن معاملتهم، وما يديرونها فيما بينهم.
Custom when it contradicts Shariah. And he said in Fath al-Qadir, in the chapter on what necessitates qada and kaffarah from the book of fasting, at the statement of al-Hidayah: 'If one eats meat between his teeth, he does not break his fast, and if it is a lot, he breaks it, and Zufar said he breaks it in both cases.' Its text: 'The verification is that the mufti in incidents must have a measure of ijtihad and knowledge of the conditions of people, and it is known that kaffarah requires complete violation, so he looks at the person of the incident: if he is one whose nature is repulsed by that, he takes the saying of Abu Yusuf, and if he is one for whom there is no effect of that, he takes the saying of Zufar.' And in Tas-hih al-Allamah Qasim: 'If you say: they might narrate statements without preference, and they might differ in correction? I say: one acts according to what they know of considering change of custom, conditions of people, what is most convenient for people, what is prevalent in dealings, and what is strong in its aspect, and existence is not devoid of distinguishing this in reality not by assumption by oneself, and the one who does not distinguish refers to the one who distinguishes for the acquittal of his responsibility.' So all this is clear in what we said about acting upon custom as long as it does not contradict Shariah, like bribes, usury, and the like. So it is necessary for the mufti, the judge, and even the mujtahid to know the conditions of people, and they said: 'Whoever is ignorant of the people of his time is ignorant.' And we have presented that they said: 'He gives fatwa according to the saying of Abu Yusuf regarding matters related to judicial decisions because he experienced incidents and knew the conditions of people.' And in al-Bahr from Manaqib al-Imam Muhammad for al-Kardari: 'Muhammad used to go to the dyers and ask about their transactions and what they revolve among themselves.'
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is a discussion from a commentary on Rasm al-Mufti, addressing the mufti's methodology regarding custom. It begins by citing a passage from Fath al-Qadir about fasting: if one eats meat stuck between teeth, according to al-Hidayah, it does not break the fast unless the amount is large; Zufar says it breaks in either case. The mufti must exercise ijtihad and know the people's conditions. For a person whose nature is repulsed by such meat, he follows Abu Yusuf (no kaffarah unless large), otherwise he follows Zufar (kaffarah always). This shows the mufti must consider the specific custom and disposition of the individual. The text then emphasizes that the mufti acts according to changing custom, people's conditions, convenience, and prevalent practice, as long as it does not contradict Shariah (e.g., bribes, riba). The mufti, qadi, and mujtahid must know their society—being ignorant of one's time is ignorance. Preference is given to Abu Yusuf's opinions in judicial matters because he experienced many cases and knew people's customs. Imam Muhammad would personally investigate market practices by visiting dyers and asking about their transactions, illustrating the importance of knowing actual customs.

Key Terms
العرف (al-urf): Custom or prevalent practice that does not contradict Shariah.
المفتي (al-mufti): One who issues fatwas; must have ijtihad and knowledge of people's conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Abu Yusuf
B) Zufar
C) Abu Hanifa
D) Muhammad al-Shaybani

Key Takeaway
A mufti must exercise ijtihad and consider people's customs, using the maxim that custom is valid unless it contradicts Shariah.

Withholding Fatwa on Higher Kharaj to Prevent Oppression
Ruling about withholding fatwa on kharaj to prevent injustice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a ruling that is known in the madhhab but not given as fatwa (lā yufatā bihī) and apply the principle of considering consequences (ma’ālāt) to determine when to withhold a ruling.

Core Idea
A technically correct ruling may be withheld if its disclosure would enable oppression.

In this passage, the early Hanafi masters discuss a nuanced rasm al-mufti principle: some rulings, though correct in theory, are deliberately not issued as fatwa. The case of higher kharaj illustrates how the potential for abuse by oppressors outweighs the benefit of publicizing a ruling. This lesson explores the reasoning behind such withholding and the broader duty of a mufti to consider consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fiqhi ruling
State the correct ruling from the madhhab: if a landowner plants a low-value crop while able to plant a high-value one, the higher kharaj is due.
2
Understand the rasm rule
Recognize that the early scholars said this ruling is 'known but not given as fatwa' (yu‘lamu wa lā yufatā bihī). Ask why they chose to withhold it.
3
Follow the objection
Examine the objection from al-‘Inayah: concealing a correct ruling seems impermissible; if authorities took the higher kharaj, it would be justified because it is obligatory.
4
Analyze the response
Understand the answer: if the ruling becomes known, every oppressor would falsely claim that land was previously planted with high-value crops (e.g., saffron) to demand higher kharaj, leading to widespread injustice.
5
Extract the principle
Conclude that a mufti must consider consequences (ma’ālāt) and real-world circumstances (‘urf, qarā’in). Rigid adherence to transmitted texts without such consideration causes oppression.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالوا: إذا زرع صاحب الأرض أرضه ما هو أدنى مع قدرته على الأعلى، وجب عليه خراج الأعلى، قالوا: وهذا يعلم ولا يفتى به؛ كي لا يتجرأ الظلمة على أخذ أموال الناس. قال في "العناية": وردّ بأنه كيف يجوز الكتمان؟ ولو أخذوا كان في موضعه؛ لكونه واجباً. وأجيب بأنا لو أفتينا بذلك لادّعى كل ظالم في أرض ليس شأنها ذلك أنها قبل هذا كانت تزرع الزعفران مثلا، فيأخذ خراج ذلك، وهو ظلم وعدوان. وكذا قال في فتح القدير : قالوا: لا يفتى بهذا؛ لما فيه من الظلمة على أموال المسلمين؛ إذ يدّعي كل ظالم أن الأرض تصلح الزراعة الزعفران ونحوه، وعلاجه صعب. تسلط فقد ظهر لك أن جمود المفتي أو القاضي على ظاهر المنقول، مع ترك العرف والقرائن الواضحة والجهل بأحوال الناس يلزم منه حقوق كثيرة، وظلم خلق كثيرين.
They said: If the owner of land sows in his land what is inferior while being able to sow superior, the higher kharaj is obligatory upon him. They said: This is known but fatwa is not given by it, so that oppressors do not dare to take people's property. He said in al-'Inayah: It was objected: How is concealment permissible? If they took it, it would be in its place because it is obligatory. And it was answered: If we give fatwa by that, every oppressor would claim in a land that is not like that, that previously it was planted with saffron, for example, and he would take the kharaj of that, and that is oppression and transgression. Similarly, it is said in Fath al-Qadir: They said: Fatwa is not given by this, due to the oppression it causes to Muslims' property, because every oppressor would claim that the land is suitable for cultivation of saffron and the like, and its treatment is difficult. So it has become clear to you that rigidity of the mufti or judge upon the apparent transmitted text, while abandoning custom, clear indications, and ignorance of people's circumstances, results in many rights being lost and oppression of many creatures.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage discusses a rasm al-mufti rule: a technically correct ruling may be withheld from fatwa to prevent its misuse by oppressors. The case is about kharaj: if a landowner could plant a high-value crop but plants a low-value one, the higher kharaj is due. However, the early scholars said this ruling is known but not given as fatwa, because if it becomes public, every oppressor will claim that his land was previously planted with saffron (a high-value crop) and demand higher kharaj, leading to widespread injustice. The objection from al-'Inayah is that concealment seems wrong since the ruling is obligatory, but the answer is that the harm of enabling oppression outweighs the benefit of publicizing the ruling. The passage then warns that a mufti or judge who rigidly follows the transmitted text without considering custom, clear circumstances, and people's situations will cause many rights to be lost and oppress many. This is a key principle: fatwa must consider the ma'alat (consequences) and the potential for abuse.

Key Terms
خراج الأعلى (kharāj al-a‘lā): The higher land tax imposed on land capable of producing high-value crops such as saffron.
لا يفتى به (lā yufatā bihī): A ruling that is known in the madhhab but is not issued as a fatwa due to potential harm or abuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Customary Practice as a Proof: The Maxim and Its Effects
Introduces the qawida with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi legal maxim that customary practice is a proof, and explain its two effects: abandoning analogy and specifying texts.

Core Idea
Customary practice is a binding proof: it overrides analogy and can specify a text, but cannot abandon it.

In this passage from al-Dhakhira, the author presents a fundamental rule of the Hanafi school: customary practice (ta'amul) is a legal proof (hujja) that has two powerful effects — it can override analogical reasoning (qiyas) and it can specify the application of a general legal text (athar). However, there is a crucial limit: custom can only specify, never abandon, a text. This lesson unpacks this maxim and its implications for the mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Maxim
Locate the sentence in the Arabic text that states: 'التعامل حجة يترك به القياس ويخص به الأثر'. This is the core rule.
2
Understand the Scope
Recognize that this maxim applies primarily in muamalat (transactions), not in pure worship.
Hanafis consider custom as a source of law in worldly matters.
3
Distinguish the Two Functions
The maxim has two parts: (1) abandoning analogy (yutraku bihi al-qiyas) and (2) specifying the text (yukhasu bihi al-athar). Understand that these are separate operations.
4
Note the Limitation
The author emphasizes that custom can only specify, not abandon, a text. Abandonment would occur if the custom contradicts a text and the text is no longer applied anywhere.
This is the key boundary condition for the mufti.
5
Connect to the Examples
Review the two examples given: the weaver lease and istisna'. Both are cases where custom led to specification, not abandonment.
These will be explored in more detail in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواز تخصيص الأثر بالتعامل لا تركه] قال في "الذخيرة" في الفصل الثامن من الإجارات في مسألة ما لو دفع إلى حائك غزلا لينسجه بالثلث ومشايخ بلخ كنصير بن يحيى، ومحمد بن سلمة، وغيرهما، كانوا يُجيزون هذه الإجارة في الثياب؛ لتعامل أهل بلدهم في الثياب، والتعامل حجة يترك به القياس، ويخص به الأثر. وتجويز هذه الإجارة في الثياب للتعامل، بمعنى تخصيص النص الذي وَرَدَ في قفيز الطحان؛ لأن النص ورد في قفيز الطحان لا في الحائك، إلا أن الحائك نظيره فيكون وارداً فيه دلالةً، فمتى تركنا العمل بدلالة هذا النص في الحائك، وعملنا بالنص في قفيز الطحان كان تخصيصا لا تركاً أصلا، وتخصيص النص بالتعامل جائز. ألا ترى أنا جوّزنا الاستصناع للتعامل، والاستصناع بيع ما ليس عنده، وإنه منهي عنه وتجويز الاستصناع بالتعامل تخصيص منا للنص الذي ورد في النهي عن بيع ما ليس عند الإنسان، لا ترك للنص أصلا؛ لأنا عملنا بالنص في غير الاستصناع. قالوا: وهذا بخلاف ما لو تعامل أهل بلدة قفيز الطحان؛ فإنه لا يجوز، ولا تكون معاملتهم معتبرة؛ لأنا لو اعتبرنا معاملتهم كان تركاً للنص أصلا، وبالتعامل لا يجوز ترك النصّ أصلا، وإنما يجوز تخصيصه، ولكن مشايخنا لم يجوزوا هذا التخصيص؛ لأن ذلك تعامل أهل بلدة واحدة، وتعامل أهل بلدة واحدة لا يخص الأثر؛ لأن تعامل أهل بلدة إن أن يجوز التخصيص، فترك التعامل من أهل بلدة أخرى يمنع التخصيص، فلا يثبت التخصيص بالشك، بخلاف التعامل في الاستصناع، فإنه وجد في البلاد كلها. انتهى كلام "الذخيرة".
Permissibility of specifying the text by customary practice, not abandoning it. He said in al-Dhakhira, in the eighth chapter of Ijarat, regarding the issue of someone giving yarn to a weaver to weave it for a third (share): The scholars of Balkh, like Nasir ibn Yahya, Muhammad ibn Salama, and others, used to permit this lease in cloth due to the customary practice of the people of their town in cloth. Customary practice is a proof by which analogy is abandoned and by which the text is specified. The permission of this lease in cloth due to customary practice means specifying the text that came concerning the qafiz of the miller, because the text came concerning the qafiz of the miller, not concerning the weaver, except that the weaver is analogous to it, so it applies to it by implication. When we abandon acting upon the implication of this text in the weaver and act upon the text in the qafiz of the miller, it is specification, not abandonment at all, and specification of the text by customary practice is permissible. Do you not see that we permitted istisna' due to customary practice, while istisna' is selling what one does not possess, and it is prohibited? Allowing istisna' by customary practice is a specification by us of the text that came prohibiting selling what one does not possess, not an abandonment of the text at all, because we act upon the text in other than istisna'. They said: This is unlike if the people of a town practice (the transaction of) the miller's qafiz; then it is not permissible, and their practice is not considered, because if we considered their practice, it would be an abandonment of the text entirely, and by customary practice it is not permissible to abandon the text entirely; rather, specification is permissible. But our scholars did not permit this specification because that is the customary practice of the people of a single town, and the customary practice of a single town does not specify the text, because the customary practice of a town—if it permits specification, then the lack of practice by the people of another town prevents specification, so specification is not established by doubt, unlike the practice in istisna', as it existed in all lands. End of the words of al-Dhakhira.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage presents a rasm rule: customary practice (ta'amul) can specify a legal text but cannot abandon it. The author cites al-Dhakhira's discussion of a lease where a weaver is hired with a share of the cloth. The scholars of Balkh allowed it based on their local custom, arguing that custom is a proof that overrides analogy (qiyas) and specifies the text. The text in question is the prohibition of the miller's qafiz (a type of sharecropping), which by analogy would also apply to the weaver. However, since the custom of the town was to engage in such leases, they specified the text to exclude the weaver, thereby not abandoning the text but limiting its scope. The author then contrasts this with the case of a single-town custom that contradicts a text: if only one town practices something contrary to a text, it is not permitted because it would amount to abandoning the text, not specifying it. Specification requires widespread custom, as seen in istisna' (manufacturing contract) which was practiced in all lands. The Hanafi position is that custom is a hujja (proof) for specification, but only if it does not lead to outright abandonment of a definitive text.

Key Terms
تعامل (ta'amul): Customary practice or common usage among people in transactions
تخصيص (takhsis): Specification; limiting the application of a general text to a subset of its apparent meaning
أثر (athar): A legal text (nass) from the Quran or Hadith, or a ruling established by them

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the key condition for customary practice to specify a text?
A) It must be practiced by at least one town.
B) It must not lead to the complete abandonment of the text.
C) It must be approved by the ruler.
D) It must be based on a hadith.

Key Takeaway
Customary practice can specify a text but never abandon it; widespread custom is required for valid specification.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Specification vs Abandonment: The Condition of Widespread Custom
Analyses the distinction between specification and abandonment, focusing on the condition of widespread custom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between specification and abandonment of a text by custom, and apply the Hanafi condition that only widespread custom can specify.

Core Idea
A local custom that contradicts a text is invalid because it abandons the text; only widespread custom can specify without abandoning.

The previous lesson introduced the maxim that custom can specify a text. But not every custom qualifies. In this passage, al-Dhakhira draws a sharp line: if the custom of a single town contradicts a text, it is not allowed, because it would amount to abandoning the text rather than specifying it. The key difference is that specification requires the text to remain operative in other contexts, while abandonment discards it entirely. This lesson examines the condition of widespread practice and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Recall the Permitted Examples
The weaver lease and istisna' are cases where custom specified the text because they did not contradict the text entirely; they only limited its scope.
2
Consider the Hypothetical Counterexample
What if a town customarily practiced the miller's qafiz (the forbidden transaction)? The author says this is not allowed.
This is a direct contradiction, not a specification.
3
Identify the Reasoning
If we follow the single-town custom, we would be abandoning the text altogether, because the text is specifically about the miller's qafiz. There is no other context to apply it.
Abandonment vs specification: the text must remain applicable somewhere.
4
Understand the Condition of Widespread Practice
The author contrasts with istisna', which was practiced in all lands. That made it reliable, not doubtful. Single-town custom is doubtful, and certainty cannot be removed by doubt.
The maxim 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk' applies.
5
Apply to Fatwa Practice
As a mufti, when a custom is presented, you must first determine whether it is widespread or local. If local and contradicts a text, it cannot be used to specify.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواز تخصيص الأثر بالتعامل لا تركه] قال في "الذخيرة" في الفصل الثامن من الإجارات في مسألة ما لو دفع إلى حائك غزلا لينسجه بالثلث ومشايخ بلخ كنصير بن يحيى، ومحمد بن سلمة، وغيرهما، كانوا يُجيزون هذه الإجارة في الثياب؛ لتعامل أهل بلدهم في الثياب، والتعامل حجة يترك به القياس، ويخص به الأثر. وتجويز هذه الإجارة في الثياب للتعامل، بمعنى تخصيص النص الذي وَرَدَ في قفيز الطحان؛ لأن النص ورد في قفيز الطحان لا في الحائك، إلا أن الحائك نظيره فيكون وارداً فيه دلالةً، فمتى تركنا العمل بدلالة هذا النص في الحائك، وعملنا بالنص في قفيز الطحان كان تخصيصا لا تركاً أصلا، وتخصيص النص بالتعامل جائز. ألا ترى أنا جوّزنا الاستصناع للتعامل، والاستصناع بيع ما ليس عنده، وإنه منهي عنه وتجويز الاستصناع بالتعامل تخصيص منا للنص الذي ورد في النهي عن بيع ما ليس عند الإنسان، لا ترك للنص أصلا؛ لأنا عملنا بالنص في غير الاستصناع. قالوا: وهذا بخلاف ما لو تعامل أهل بلدة قفيز الطحان؛ فإنه لا يجوز، ولا تكون معاملتهم معتبرة؛ لأنا لو اعتبرنا معاملتهم كان تركاً للنص أصلا، وبالتعامل لا يجوز ترك النصّ أصلا، وإنما يجوز تخصيصه، ولكن مشايخنا لم يجوزوا هذا التخصيص؛ لأن ذلك تعامل أهل بلدة واحدة، وتعامل أهل بلدة واحدة لا يخص الأثر؛ لأن تعامل أهل بلدة إن أن يجوز التخصيص، فترك التعامل من أهل بلدة أخرى يمنع التخصيص، فلا يثبت التخصيص بالشك، بخلاف التعامل في الاستصناع، فإنه وجد في البلاد كلها. انتهى كلام "الذخيرة".
Permissibility of specifying the text by customary practice, not abandoning it. He said in al-Dhakhira, in the eighth chapter of Ijarat, regarding the issue of someone giving yarn to a weaver to weave it for a third (share): The scholars of Balkh, like Nasir ibn Yahya, Muhammad ibn Salama, and others, used to permit this lease in cloth due to the customary practice of the people of their town in cloth. Customary practice is a proof by which analogy is abandoned and by which the text is specified. The permission of this lease in cloth due to customary practice means specifying the text that came concerning the qafiz of the miller, because the text came concerning the qafiz of the miller, not concerning the weaver, except that the weaver is analogous to it, so it applies to it by implication. When we abandon acting upon the implication of this text in the weaver and act upon the text in the qafiz of the miller, it is specification, not abandonment at all, and specification of the text by customary practice is permissible. Do you not see that we permitted istisna' due to customary practice, while istisna' is selling what one does not possess, and it is prohibited? Allowing istisna' by customary practice is a specification by us of the text that came prohibiting selling what one does not possess, not an abandonment of the text at all, because we act upon the text in other than istisna'. They said: This is unlike if the people of a town practice (the transaction of) the miller's qafiz; then it is not permissible, and their practice is not considered, because if we considered their practice, it would be an abandonment of the text entirely, and by customary practice it is not permissible to abandon the text entirely; rather, specification is permissible. But our scholars did not permit this specification because that is the customary practice of the people of a single town, and the customary practice of a single town does not specify the text, because the customary practice of a town—if it permits specification, then the lack of practice by the people of another town prevents specification, so specification is not established by doubt, unlike the practice in istisna', as it existed in all lands. End of the words of al-Dhakhira.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage presents a rasm rule: customary practice (ta'amul) can specify a legal text but cannot abandon it. The author cites al-Dhakhira's discussion of a lease where a weaver is hired with a share of the cloth. The scholars of Balkh allowed it based on their local custom, arguing that custom is a proof that overrides analogy (qiyas) and specifies the text. The text in question is the prohibition of the miller's qafiz (a type of sharecropping), which by analogy would also apply to the weaver. However, since the custom of the town was to engage in such leases, they specified the text to exclude the weaver, thereby not abandoning the text but limiting its scope. The author then contrasts this with the case of a single-town custom that contradicts a text: if only one town practices something contrary to a text, it is not permitted because it would amount to abandoning the text, not specifying it. Specification requires widespread custom, as seen in istisna' (manufacturing contract) which was practiced in all lands. The Hanafi position is that custom is a hujja (proof) for specification, but only if it does not lead to outright abandonment of a definitive text.

Key Terms
تعامل (ta'amul): Customary practice or common usage among people in transactions
تخصيص (takhsis): Specification; limiting the application of a general text to a subset of its apparent meaning
أثر (athar): A legal text (nass) from the Quran or Hadith, or a ruling established by them

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the single-town custom of the miller's qafiz not allowed?
A) Because it is not practiced in all lands.
B) Because it would lead to abandonment of the text.
C) Because the miller's qafiz is prohibited by consensus.
D) Because the custom is not proven.

Key Takeaway
A custom that contradicts a text is only acceptable if it specifies without abandoning; single-town customs are doubtful and cannot override certain texts.
