The Ruling on Considering General and Specific Custom in Fatwa
Rasm al-Mufti rule on custom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that general custom can specify a nass but not abandon it, and identify when specific custom is considered.

Core Idea
General custom specifies nass; specific custom binds only its people and cannot override nass.

A mufti must know when to invoke custom. This passage from a rasm al-mufti text gives precise conditions: general custom can specify a text, but not abandon it; specific custom is only binding among its people. We will analyse the rule and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of custom
Distinguish between general custom (urf amm) which is widespread, and specific custom (urf khass) which is limited to a group or locality.
General custom can specify a nass; specific custom cannot abandon or specify a nass.
2
Apply the rule for general custom
Check if the custom leads to abandoning (tark) the nass – if so, it is not considered. If it leads to specification (takhsis), it is considered.
Specification limits but does not contradict the nass.
3
Apply the rule for specific custom
Specific custom is not considered for those outside the community. For its people, it is considered only if it does not lead to abandoning or specifying a nass, even if it contradicts the apparent ruling (zahir al-riwaya).
Among its people, it can override the apparent ruling but not a nass.
4
Apply to examples
In oaths and contracts, interpret words according to local custom. The speaker's intent is based on his custom, not the jurists' technical definitions.
The mufti must ascertain the customary meaning in the locality.
5
Note the hierarchy
Nass > urf amm with specification > urf khass among its people (only if no conflict with nass).
This hierarchy guides the mufti's decision.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحاصل أن العرف العام لا يعتبر إذا لزم منه ترك المنصوص، وإنما يعتبر إذا لزم منه تخصيص النصّ والعرف الخاص لا يعتبر في الموضعين، وإنما يعتبر في حق أهله فقط إذا لم يلزم منه ترك النص ولا تخصيصه، وإن خالف ظاهر الرواية. وذلك كما في الألفاظ المتعارفة في الأيمان والعادة الجارية في العقود، من بيع وإجارة ونحوها، فتجري تلك الألفاظ والعقود في كل بلدة على عادة أهلها ويراد منها ذلك المعتاد بينهم، ويعاملون دون غيرهم بما يقتضيه ذلك من صحة وفساد وتحريم وتحليل، وغير ذلك، وإن صرّح الفقهاء بأن مقتضاه خلاف ما اقتضاه العرف؛ لأن المتكلم إنما يتكلم على عرفه وعادته ويقصد ذلك بكلامه دون ما أراده الفقهاء، إنما يعامل كل أحد بما أراده والألفاظ العرفية حقائق اصطلاحية يصير بها المعنى الأصلي كالمجاز اللغوي، قال في "جامع الفصولين": مطلق الكلام فيما بين الناس ينصرف إلى المتعارف". وفي "فتاوى العلامة قاسم: التحقيق أن لفظ الواقف، والموصي، والحالف، والناذر، وكل عاقد يحمل على عادته في خطابه ولغته التي يتكلم بها، وافقت لغة العرب ولغة الشارع أو لا". ثم اعلم أني لم أر من تكلّم على هذه المسألة بما يشفي العليل، وكشفها يحتاج إلى زيادة تطويل؛ لأن الكلام عليها يطول؛ لاحتياجه إلى ذكر فروع وأصول وأجوبة عمّا عسى يقال وتوضيح ما بنى على هذا المقال فاقتصرت هناك على ما ذكرته ثم أظهرت بعض ما أضمرته في رسالة جعلتها شرحا لهذا البيت وضمنتها بعض ما عنيت، وسميتها "نشر العرف في بناء بعض الأحكام على العُرف"، فمن رام الزيادة على ذلك، فليرجع إلى ما هنالك.
The conclusion is that general custom is not considered if it necessitates abandoning the text; rather it is considered if it necessitates specification of the text. And specific custom is not considered in either case; rather it is considered only with respect to its people if it does not necessitate abandoning the text nor specifying it, even if it contradicts the apparent ruling. That is as in customary expressions in oaths and the prevailing practice in contracts, like sale, lease, and the like. So those expressions and contracts proceed in every town according to the custom of its people, and what is customary among them is intended, and they are dealt with accordingly, and not others, by what necessitates validity, invalidity, prohibition, permissibility, etc., even if the jurists have stated that the requirement is contrary to what custom requires; because the speaker speaks according to his custom and habit, and intends that by his speech, not what the jurists intended. Rather, everyone is dealt with according to what he intended, and customary expressions are technical realities by which the original meaning becomes like a linguistic metaphor. He said in Jami' al-Fusulayn: 'Absolute speech among people is directed to what is customary.' And in Fatawa al-Allama Qasim: 'The reality is that the utterance of the waqif, the bequeather, the swearer, the nazir, and every contractant is construed according to his custom in his speech and language that he speaks, whether it agrees with the language of the Arabs and the language of the Lawgiver or not.' Then know that I have not seen anyone who spoke on this issue in a way that heals the ailment, and revealing it requires additional lengthening; because speech about it becomes lengthy due to needing to mention branches, principles, answers to what might be said, and clarification of what is built on this discourse. So I confined myself there to what I mentioned, then I revealed some of what I concealed in a treatise that I made a commentary on this verse and incorporated some of what I intended, and called it 'Nashr al-Urf fi Bina' Ba'd al-Ahkam ala al-Urf.' Whoever seeks more than that, let him refer to that.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage establishes a rule for the mufti regarding the consideration of custom (urf). It distinguishes between general custom (al-urf al-amm) and specific custom (al-urf al-khass). General custom is not accepted if it contradicts a clear textual ruling (nass) by abandoning it entirely, but it is accepted if it merely specifies the text (takhsis), making it more precise. Specific custom is not accepted in either case for those outside the community, but it is accepted among the people of that custom if it does not lead to abandoning or specifying a text, even if it goes against the apparent ruling (zahir al-riwaya). The author gives examples: in oaths and contracts, words are interpreted according to the custom of the locality, and contracts like sale and lease are governed by local practice. This is because a person’s intent is based on his custom, not the technical definitions of jurists. He cites Jami' al-Fusulayn and a fatwa of Qasim, emphasizing that the language of a waqf founder, testator, oath-taker, vow-maker, and any contracting party is interpreted according to their custom, regardless of whether it matches classical Arabic or legal terminology. The author notes that this topic is complex and he has elaborated in a separate treatise called 'Nashr al-Urf.'

Key Terms
عرف عام (urf amm): Custom that is widespread and not restricted to a specific group or locality.
عرف خاص (urf khass): Custom limited to a particular group, profession, or locality.
نص (nass): A definitive textual ruling from the Quran or hadith that is not open to interpretation.
تخصيص (takhsis): Specification of a general ruling by a specific evidence.
الظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The apparent ruling from the canonical Hanafi texts (the six books of Imam Muhammad).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is specific custom (urf khass) considered?
A) Always, even if it abandons a nass.
B) Only among its people, provided it does not abandon or specify a nass.
C) Only if it is approved by the majority of jurists.
D) Never, because it contradicts the apparent ruling.

Key Takeaway
General custom can specify a nass but not abandon it; specific custom binds only its people and cannot override a nass, even if it contradicts the apparent ruling.

Acting and Giving Fatwa by Weak Opinions
Ruling on acting and issuing fatwa by weak opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a marjuh opinion is prohibited for fatwa and personal practice except in cases of necessity.

Core Idea
A marjuh opinion is treated as non-existent; only necessity permits its use.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on acting by and issuing fatwa with weak (marjuh) opinions. The default position is complete prohibition—a marjuh is like an abrogated ruling. However, the school recognizes genuine necessity (darurah) as a valid exception, as illustrated by a specific case from Abu Yusuf. This lesson unpacks the principle, the inter-madhhab dispute, and the practical application for muftis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
From the matn and commentary, state the general rule: acting by a marjuh opinion is not permissible (la yajuz) for fatwa, judgment, or personal practice.
The passage explicitly says 'wa la yajuz bi al-da'if al-'amal' and prohibits answering a questioner with it.
2
Understand the justification: marjuh as non-existent
The marjuh is treated 'bimanzila al-'adam' (like non-existence) when compared to the rajih. Some scholars analogize it to an abrogated ruling (mansukh). Recognize when this analogy applies (retraction or known sequence) and when it does not (e.g., opinions of different imams).
The commentary refines: the analogy holds when one of two sayings is definitively chosen; otherwise, it means the marjuh is simply not acted upon.
3
Recognize the exception: darurah
The default prohibition is lifted when there is a genuine necessity. The passage gives an example: a traveler or guest who fears suspicion (riba) may follow Abu Yusuf's weak opinion on ghusl.
Necessity justifies acting on the marjuh for oneself, but not for giving fatwa to others or for judicial rulings.
4
Distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i (Subki)
According to al-Subki, the Shafi'i school allows acting on a weak opinion for oneself but not for fatwa or judgment. The Hanafi school prohibits even personal practice unless there is necessity. This difference stems from treating the marjuh as 'like non-existent' in Hanafi usul.
The commentary resolves apparent contradiction: the reported consensus refers to acting out of caprice, not necessity.
5
Apply the rule to a concrete case
Consider the example: a traveler who had a wet dream and held his penis until desire subsided. According to the rajih, ghusl is required. But due to necessity (fear of suspicion), Abu Yusuf's weak opinion (no ghusl) may be followed. This illustrates the exception.
The mufti must not give this as a general fatwa, but can inform the individual that he may act on it due to necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز بالضعيف العمل إلا لعامل له ضروره ولا به يجاب من جاء يسأل أو من له معرفة مشهوره لكنما القاضي به لا يقضي وإن قضى فحكمه لا يمضي لا سيّما قضاتُنا إذْ قُيّدوا براجح المذهب حين قلدوا وتم ما نظمته في سلك والحمد لله ختام مسك الإفتاء والعمل على الضعيف قدمنا أول الشرح عن العلامة قاسم: أن الحكم والفتيا بما هو مرجوح خلاف الإجماع، وأن المرجوح في مقابلة الراجح بمنزلة العدم، والترجيح بغير مرجّح في المتقابلات ممنوع، وأن من يكتفي بأن يكون فتواه أو عمله موافقا لقول أو وجه في المسألة، ويعمل بما شاء من الأقوال والوجوه من غير نظر في الترجيح، فقد جهل وخرق الإجماع. وقدمنا هناك نحوه عن فتاوى العلامة ابن الشرنبلالي في رسالته "العقد الفريد في جواز التقليد": مقتضى مذهب الشافعي كما قاله السبكي: منع العمل بالقول المرجوح في القضاء والإفتاء دون العمل لنفسه. ومذهب الحنفية: المنع عن المرجوح لنفسه؛ لكون المرجوح صار منسوخا. حتى قلت التعليل بأنه صار منسوخاً إنما يظهر فيما لو كان في المسألة قولان، رجع المجتهد عن أحدهما، أو علم تأخر أحدهما عن الآخر، وإلا فلا، كما لو كان في المسألة قول لأبي يوسف وقول لمحمد، فإنه لا يظهر فيه النسخ، لكن مراده أنه إذا صحح أحدهما صار الآخر بمنزلة المنسوخ. وهو معنى ما مر من قول العلامة قاسم: "إن المرجوح في مقابلة الراجح بمنزلة العدم". ثم إن ما ذكره السبكي من جواز العمل بالمرجوح في حق نفسه عند الشافعي، مخالف لما مر عن العلامة قاسم، وقدّمنا مثله أول الشرح عن فتاوى ابن حجر من نقل الإجماع على عدم الإفتاء والعمل بما شاء من الأقوال، إلا أن يقال : المراد بالعمل الحكم والقضاء، وهو بعيد. والأظهر في الجواب أخذاً من التعبير بالتشهي مهما أراد من الأقوال في أي وقت أراد، أما لو عمل بالضعيف في بعض الأوقات لضرورة اقتضت ذلك، فلا يمنع منه. وعليه يحمل ما تقدم عن الشرنبلالي: "أن مذهب الحنفية المنع"، بدليل أنهم أجازوا للمسافر والضيف الذي خاف الريبة أن يأخذ بقول أبي يوسف بعدم وجوب الغسل على المحتلم الذي أمسك ذكره عند ما أحس بالاحتلام إلى أن فترت شهوته ثم أرسله، مع أن قوله هذا خلاف الراجح في المذهب، لكن أجازوا الأخذ به للضرورة.
And it is not permissible to act by the weak (opinion) except for an actor who has a necessity, nor is it answered by it the one who comes asking, or one who has knowledge of its well-known (opinion). But the judge does not judge by it, and if he judges, his judgment does not pass, especially our judges since they are restricted to the preponderant of the madhhab when they followed. And complete is what I have composed in a string, and praise be to Allah, the seal of musk. [Section: Issuing fatwa and acting by the weak] We presented at the beginning of the commentary, from the scholar Qasim: that ruling and giving fatwa by what is marjuh is contrary to consensus, and that the marjuh in comparison to the rajih is like non-existence, and preponderance without a preponderating factor in opposites is prohibited, and that whoever is satisfied that his fatwa or action agrees with a saying or a view in the matter, and acts by whatever sayings and views he wishes without consideration of preponderance, has indeed been ignorant and breached consensus. And we presented there something similar from the fatwas of the scholar Ibn Hajar, but in it also: Imam al-Subki said in the Waqf from his fatwas: It is permissible to follow the weak view in reality with respect to action concerning oneself, not in fatwa and judgment, for Ibn al-Salah transmitted consensus that it is not permissible. And the scholar al-Shurunbulali said in his treatise "al-'Iqd al-Farid fi Jawaz al-Taqlid": The implication of the Shafi'i school, as al-Subki said, is prohibition of acting by the marjuh saying in judgment and fatwa, but not in action for oneself. And the Hanafi school: prohibition of the marjuh for oneself, because the marjuh has become like abrogated. Even I said: The reasoning that it has become abrogated only appears in a case where there are two sayings in the matter, and the mujtahid retracted one of them, or the later of the two is known, otherwise not, as if there is a saying of Abu Yusuf and a saying of Muhammad, for abrogation does not appear in it. But his intent is that when one of them is authenticated, the other becomes in the position of the abrogated. That is the meaning of what passed from the scholar Qasim: "The marjuh in comparison to the rajih is like non-existence." Then what al-Subki mentioned about the permissibility of acting by the marjuh for oneself according to al-Shafi'i is contrary to what passed from the scholar Qasim, and we presented its like at the beginning of the commentary from the fatwas of Ibn Hajar from the transmission of consensus on the prohibition of giving fatwa and acting by whatever sayings one wishes, unless it is said: the intended meaning of action is judgment and ruling, which is unlikely. And the more apparent in the answer, taking from the expression of following desire, is that it is whenever he wishes from the sayings at whatever time he wishes. As for acting by the weak in some times due to a necessity that necessitated that, then it is not prevented. And upon this is carried what preceded from al-Shurunbulali: "that the Hanafi school is prohibition," evidenced by the fact that they permitted for the traveler and the guest who fears suspicion (riba) to take the saying of Abu Yusuf about the non-obligation of ghusl for the one who had a wet dream and held his penis when he felt the dream until his desire subsided then released it, even though this saying of his is contrary to the preponderant in the madhhab, but they permitted acting by it due to necessity.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on when it is permissible to act by or give fatwa with a weak (marjuh) opinion in the Hanafi school. The text begins by quoting the matn's lines: acting by a weak opinion is not allowed except for someone who has a necessity, and it is not used to answer a questioner, nor may a judge judge by it. The commentary then expands on this rule by presenting various scholarly positions. It first references the scholar Qasim, who states that giving a ruling or fatwa by a marjuh opinion is contrary to consensus, and the marjuh is treated as non-existent compared to the rajih. He criticizes those who pick and choose any opinion without considering preponderance. Then it mentions Ibn Hajar's fatwas, where al-Subki is quoted as saying that in the Shafi'i school, following a weak view is permissible for one's own personal practice but not for fatwa or judgment, based on Ibn al-Salah's reported consensus. Al-Shurunbulali's treatise clarifies that for the Shafi'is, prohibition applies only to fatwa and judgment, while for the Hanafis, the prohibition extends to personal practice as well, because the marjuh becomes like an abrogated ruling. The commentator then critically refines this: the analogy of abrogation (naskh) only holds when there is a known retraction or temporal sequence, not when the differing opinions come from different imams like Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. However, the intended meaning is that once a position is deemed rajih, the other is treated as if abrogated, consistent with Qasim's statement. The text then resolves an apparent contradiction: al-Subki's permission for personal practice seems to conflict with the earlier claim of consensus. The commentator suggests that the consensus refers to acting out of caprice (tashahhi), i.e., picking any opinion at any time without reason. However, if one acts on a weak opinion occasionally due to a genuine necessity, it is not prohibited. This is illustrated by a Hanafi example: a traveler or guest who fears suspicion (riba) may follow Abu Yusuf's opinion that ghusl is not obligatory for a person who, after experiencing a wet dream, holds his penis until his desire subsides and then releases it. Although Abu Yusuf's opinion is weak in the madhhab, the school permits acting on it in case of necessity, showing that the prohibition is not absolute when there is a valid excuse.

Key Terms
مرجوح (marjuh): A legal opinion that is deemed weaker or preponderated against in the madhhab
راجح (rajih): The preponderant opinion within the madhhab
ضرورة (darurah): Necessity that justifies an exception to the general prohibition of acting on weak opinions

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is it permissible for a Hanafi to act by a weak (marjuh) opinion?
A) At any time one chooses
B) Only for giving fatwa, not for personal practice
C) Only when there is a necessity (darurah)
D) Never, under any circumstance

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a marjuh opinion is not to be acted upon or used in fatwa or judgment, except when there is a genuine necessity.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
Acting Upon and Issuing Fatwa with Weak Opinions Under Necessity
Permissibility of using weak opinions under necessity in Hanafi ifta

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a Hanafi mufti may issue a fatwa based on a weak (daʿīf/shādhdh) opinion and apply the rule to a given scenario.

Core Idea
A weak opinion may be used under genuine necessity for ease, but not casually.

In Hanafi rasm al-mufti, the standard is to issue fatwa from the strongest (mashhūr) opinion. However, this passage introduces a critical refinement: under genuine necessity (ḍarūra), both the mufti and the layperson may resort to a weak (daʿīf or even shādhdh) opinion that provides ease. This lesson examines the basis, conditions, and limits of this exception, including the important case of takfīr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and its exception
State the default rule: weak opinions are not normally used. Then identify the exception: necessity (ḍarūra) permits acting on and issuing fatwa with weak opinions.
The general rule is expressed as: 'ليس له العمل بالضعيف ولا الإفتاء به' — 'He may not act upon the weak nor issue fatwa with it.'
2
Analyze the authority behind the weak opinion
Recognize that the weak opinion (non-flowing blood does not nullify wudu) is held by Imam al-Marghinani, a scholar of the highest rank (aṣḥāb al-takhrīj wa al-taṣḥīḥ). Even though it is shādhdh (isolated), his authority gives it weight under necessity.
Al-Marghinani's status means his opinion is not treated as a mere personal view; it is within the madhhab's methodology.
3
Examine the conditions for using the weak opinion
The weak opinion may be used only when there is genuine necessity (ḍarūra) — severe hardship that cannot be removed without extraordinary effort. In the author's case, washing and bandaging at every prayer caused great difficulty.
Necessity must be real; convenience is not enough. The mufti seeks 'taysīr' (ease) for the one in need.
4
Apply the rule to a practical scenario
Consider the author's example: he followed al-Marghinani's weak opinion during his illness, and after recovery he repeated all prayers performed under that fatwa. This shows that using a weak opinion under necessity does not make the act permanently valid; if possible, recompense is required.
This step highlights that the exception is temporary and tied to the necessity.
5
Distinguish the takfīr exception
Note that in matters of takfīr (declaring a Muslim an unbeliever), even a weak opinion that suggests kufr is avoided, and the stronger opinion (preserving Islam) is followed. This is because of the gravity of kufr.
This shows that not all weak opinions are used under necessity; the subject matter matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وينبغي أن يكون الإفتاء والعمل على الضعيف من هذا القبيل ما ذكره الإمام المرغيناني صاحب "الهداية" في كتابه مختارات "النوازل" - وهو كتاب مشهور ينقل عنه شراح "الهداية" وغيرهم حيث قال في فصل النجاسة: "والدم إذا خرج من القروح قليلا قليلا غير سائل فذاك ليس بمانع وإن كثر. وقيل: لو كان بحال لو تركه لسال، يمنع ثم أعاد المسألة في نواقض الوضوء، فقال: "ولو خرج منه شيء قليل ومسحه بخرقة حتى لو ترك يسيل لا ينقض. وقيل: إلخ." .... وقد راجعت نسخة أخرى، فرأيت العبارة فيها كذلك. ولا يخفى أن المشهور في عامة كتب المذهب هو القول الثاني المعبّر عنه بـ"قيل". وأما ما اختاره من القول الأول، فلم أَرَ من سبقه إليه، ولا من تابعه عليه بعد المراجعة الكثيرة، فهو قول شاذ ولكن صاحب "الهداية" إمام جليل من أعظم مشايخ المذهب، من طبقة أصحاب التخريج والتصحيح، كما مر فيجوز للمعذور تقليده في هذا القول عند الضرورة، فإن فيه توسعة عظيمة لأهل الأعذار كما بينته في رسالتي المسماة "الأحكام المخصصة بكي الحمّصة". وقد كنت ابتليتُ مدّة بكي الحمّصة، ولم أجد ما تصح به صلاتي على مذهبنا بلا مشقة إلا على هذا القول؛ لأن الخارج منه وإن كان قليلاً لكنه لو ترك يسيل، وهو نجس وناقض للطهارة على القول المشهور خلافا لما قاله بعضهم كما قد بيّنته في الرسالة المذكورة، ولا يصير به صاحب عذر؛ لأنه يمكن دفع العذر بالغسل والربط بنحو جلدة مانعة للسيلان عند كل صلاة، كما كنت أفعله، ولكن فيه مشقة وحرج عظيم، فاضطررت إلى تقليد هذا القول، ثم لما عافاني الله تعالى منه أعدت صلاة تلك المدة. والله تعالى الحمد. وقد ذكر صاحب "البحر" في الحيض في بحث ألوان الدماء أقوالاً ضعيفةً، ثم قال: وفي "المعراج" عن فخر الأئمة: لو أفتى مفت بشيء من هذه الأقوال في مواضع الضرورة طلباً للتيسير كان حسنا. له وبه علم أن المضطرّ له العمل بذلك لنفسه كما قلنا، وأن المفتي الإفتاء به للمضطر. فما مرّ من أنه ليس له العمل بالضعيف ولا الإفتاء به محمول على غير موضع الضرورة، كما علمته من مجموع ما قررناه. والله تعالى أعلم. وينبغي أن يلحق بالضرورة أيضا ما قدمناه من أنه لا يفتى بكفر مسلم، في كفره اختلاف ولو رواية ضعيفة فقد عدلوا عن الإفتاء بالصحيح؛ لأن الكفر شيء عظيم.
And it is befitting that issuing fatwa and acting upon the weak (opinion) is of this category. Mentioned by Imam al-Marghinani, author of al-Hidayah, in his book "Mukhtarat al-Nawazil" — a well-known book from which the commentators of al-Hidayah and others transmit — where he said in the chapter on impurity: "Blood that comes out of sores little by little without flowing, that is not a preventer (of prayer) even if abundant. And it was said: If it were such that if left it would flow, it prevents." Then he repeated the issue in the nullifiers of wudu, saying: "If something little comes out of him and he wipes it with a cloth, such that if left it would flow, it does not nullify (wudu). And it was said: etc." ... And I checked another copy, and saw the wording in it as such. It is not hidden that the well-known (opinion) in most books of the madhhab is the second opinion expressed by "it was said." As for what he chose — the first opinion — I did not see anyone before him nor anyone who followed him upon it after extensive review; it is a shadhdh (isolated) opinion. But the author of al-Hidayah is a great imam from the greatest shaykhs of the madhhab, from the level of the people of takhrij and tas-hih, as has passed. So it is permissible for the excused person to follow him in this opinion when necessity arises, for in it is great expansion for those with excuses, as I explained in my treatise named "al-Ahkam al-Mukhasasa bi Kayy al-Himmasa." I myself was afflicted for a period with kayy al-himmasa, and I did not find anything by which my prayer would be valid according to our madhhab without hardship except on this opinion; because what comes out of it, even if little, if it were left it would flow, and it is impure and nullifies purification according to the well-known opinion — contrary to what some have said as I explained in the mentioned treatise — and one does not become a person with an excuse through it, because the excuse can be removed by washing and bandaging with something like a skin that prevents flow at every prayer, as I used to do, but that involved great hardship and difficulty, so I was compelled to follow this opinion. Then when Allah cured me of it, I repeated the prayers of that period. Praise be to Allah. And the author of al-Bahr mentioned in hayd, in the discussion of colors of blood, weak opinions, then said: In al-Mi'raj from Fakhr al-A'imma: If a mufti issues a fatwa with something of these opinions in places of necessity seeking ease, it would be good. From this it is known that the one in need may act upon it for himself as we said, and the mufti may issue fatwa with it for the one in need. So what has passed — that he may not act upon the weak nor issue fatwa with it — is construed as other than the case of necessity, as you have understood from the totality of what we have established. And Allah knows best. And it is befitting that also be joined to necessity what we have presented: that a Muslim is not declared an unbeliever, if there is difference of opinion (concerning his unbelief) even if based on a weak narration, for they have deviated from issuing fatwa with the sound (opinion) because unbelief is a grave matter.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti deals with a key methodological rule for muftis and laypersons: the permissibility of using weak (shadhdh or da'if) opinions when necessity (darura) demands. The author begins by recalling that Imam al-Marghinani in his work Mukhtarat al-Nawazil presented two opinions regarding blood from wounds: one that non-flowing blood does not prevent prayer or nullify wudu, and another that if it would flow if left, it does prevent/nullify. The well-known (mashhur) opinion in the Hanafi school is the second, stricter one. However, al-Marghinani chose the first, weaker opinion. After extensive research, the author finds no one before or after al-Marghinani who chose that opinion, making it isolated (shadhdh). Nevertheless, because al-Marghinani is a highly authoritative imam from the class of mujtahids capable of takhrij and tas-hih, it is permissible for a person with an excuse (ma'dhur) to follow that weak opinion when necessity arises, as it provides great ease. The author then shares his personal experience with a medical condition (kayy al-himmasa, cauterization of a smallpox pustule). The discharge, though little, would flow if left, and according to the mashhur opinion it is impure and nullifies wudu, and he could not become an excused person because he could wash and bandage it each prayer, but that caused hardship. So he followed al-Marghinani's weak opinion out of necessity, and later when cured, he repeated all prayers performed under that fatwa. This shows that following a weak opinion under necessity is allowed but does not make the act permanently valid; if possible, the duties must be repeated. The author then supports his position by quoting al-Bahr and al-Mi'raj: a mufti may issue fatwa with weak opinions in cases of necessity seeking ease. He concludes that the general rule forbidding acting upon or issuing fatwa with weak opinions applies only when there is no necessity. Finally, he adds an important exception: in matters of takfir (declaring someone an unbeliever), even a weak opinion that suggests a Muslim may be considered a kafir is avoided, and the stronger opinion preserving Islam is followed, because of the gravity of kufr.

Key Terms
الضعيف (al-daʿīf): An opinion that is not the mashhur or strongest within the madhhab; may be shadhdh (isolated) or based on a weak transmission, but still within the Hanafi school.
المعذور (al-maʿdhūr): A person who has a valid excuse (udhr) that prevents fulfilling a religious obligation in the normal way, e.g., chronic illness or incontinence.
ضرورة (ḍarūra): A situation of severe hardship or necessity that permits deviation from the standard ruling to avoid harm or extreme difficulty.
شاذ (shādhdh): An isolated opinion that is contrary to the well-known (mashhūr) view of the school, often held by a single authoritative scholar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for a mufti to issue a fatwa based on a weak (shadhdh) opinion?
A) The weak opinion must be from a Hanafi source and he may use it whenever he wishes.
B) He may use it only when the person asking is in a state of necessity and seeking ease.
C) He may use it only if the weak opinion is from a companion of the Prophet.
D) He may never use a weak opinion; only the well-known opinion is allowed.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi mufti may issue fatwa with a weak (shādhdh) opinion under genuine necessity to provide ease, but the layperson must recompense if the necessity ends.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Conditions for Acting on Weak Narrations: Personal Practice vs. Fatwa
Analyzes when a scholar may act on weak narrations for himself versus giving fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a mujtahid may act on weak narrations for himself and apply the distinction that prohibits using them in issuing fatwas.

Core Idea
A mujtahid may act on weak narrations for himself but must follow the madhhab in fatwa; the layman must follow authenticated rulings.

Islamic legal theory distinguishes between personal practice ('amal) and giving legal verdicts (ifta'). This lesson unpacks a key rasm al-mufti rule: when can a scholar rely on a weak (da'if) narration? The answer hinges on the scholar's juristic capacity and the context. We will explore the conditions that permit acting on weak narrations for oneself and the binding constraints that prevent such narrations from being used in fatwa. The passage refutes the misconception that a mufti may freely adopt weak opinions, affirming the authority of the madhhab's established positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central question
The passage begins by asking: Is it permissible for a person to act on a weak narration concerning himself? Note the frame: 'himself' versus giving fatwa to others.
This sets up the core distinction between personal practice and public fatwa.
2
Define 'one with opinion' (dhu ra'y)
The condition is having 'ra'y' – juristic insight. This is equated with being a mujtahid within the madhhab. The opposite is the layman ('ammi), who lacks this capacity.
Use the legal definition dissector to fully understand 'dhu ra'y'.
3
Apply the distinction: personal vs. fatwa
For personal practice, a mujtahid may act on weak narrations even if it contradicts his madhhab. But for fatwa, he must follow the agreed-upon positions of Abu Hanifa and his companions.
The rationale: the early imams' ijtihad is stronger, and the questioner seeks the madhhab's ruling, not the mufti's personal view.
4
Address the hypothetical objection
The passage presents an objection: 'This contradicts earlier statements that a mufti cannot deviate from the madhhab.' The response refines: that restriction applies only to fatwa, not personal practice.
This is a critical refinement – the lesson's textual operation.
5
Confirm the rule with examples
The passage cites Shafi'i practice and Ibn al-Humam's choice of Malik's opinion to illustrate that mujtahids may follow their own ijtihad personally.
These examples reinforce the principle across madhhabs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرائط العمل بالضعيف
وفي "شرح الأشباه" للبيري: هل يجوز للإنسان العمل بالضعيف من الرواية في حق نفسه؟ نعم ! إذا كان له رأي، أما إذا كان عاميا فلم أَرَه، لكن مقتضى تقييده بذي الرأي أنه لا يجوز للعامي ذلك".
قال في "خزانة الروايات": العالم الذي يعرف معنى النصوص والأخبار وهو من أهل الدراية يجوز له أن يعمل عليها، وإن كان مخالفا لمذهبه. وتقييده بذي الرأي أي المجتهد في المذهب مخرج للعامي كما قال، فإنه يلزمه اتباع ما صححوا ، لكن في غير موضع الضرورة كما علمته آنفا. فإن قلت: هذا مخالف لما قدمته سابقاً من أن المفتي المجتهد ليس له العدول عما اتفق عليه أبو حنيفة وأصحابه فليس له الإفتاء به وإن كان مجتهدا متقنا؛ لأنهم عرفوا الأدلة وميّزوا بين ما صح وثبت وبين غيره، ولا يبلغ اجتهاده اجتهادهم كما قدمناه عن "الخانية" وغيرها. قلت: ذاك في حق من يفتي غيره. ولعل وجهه أنه لما علم أن اجتهادهم أقوى ليس له أن يبني مسائل العامة على اجتهاده الأضعف، أو لأن السائل إنما جاء يستفتيه عن مذهب الإمام الذي قلده ذلك المفتي، فعليه أن يفتي بالمذهب الذي جاء المستفتي يستفتيه عنه، ولذا ذكر العلامة قاسم في فتاواه أنه سئل عن واقف شَرَطَ لنفسه التغيير والتبديل، فصيّر الوقف لزوجته. فأجاب أني لم أقف على اعتبار هذا في شيء من كتب علمائنا وليس للمفتي إلا نقل ما صح عند أهل مذهبه الذين يفتى بقولهم؛ ولأن المستفتي إنما يسأل عما ذهب إليه أئمة ذلك المذهب، لا عما ينجلي للمفتي".
وكذا نقلوا عن أئمة الشافعية: أنه كان إذا جاء أحد يستفتيه عن بيع الصبرة يقول له: تسألني عن مذهبي أو عن مذهب الشافعي؟ وكذا نقلوا عنه أنه كان أحيانا يقول: لو اجتهدت فأدى اجتهادي إلى مذهب أبي حنيفة، فأقول : مذهب الشافعي كذا، ولكنّي أقول مذهب أبي حنيفة؛ لأنه جاء ليعلم ويستفتي عن مذهب الشافعي، فلا بد أن أعرفه بأني أفتي بغيره.
وأما في حق العمل به لنفسه فالظاهر جوازه له، ويدل عليه قول "خزانة الروايات": يجوز له أن يعمل عليها وإن كان مخالفا لمذهبه". أي لأن المجتهد يلزمه اتباع ما أدى إليه اجتهاده، ولذا ترى المحقق ابن الهمام اختار مسائل خارجة عن المذهب، ومرّة رجّح في مسألة قول الإمام مالك، وقال: هذا الذي أدين به". وقدمنا عن "التحرير" "أن المجتهد في بعض المسائل على القول بتجزئ الاجتهاد وهو الحق يلزمه التقليد فيما لا يقدر عليه أي فيما لا يقدر على الاجتهاد فيه لا في غيره.
Conditions for acting on the weak [narration]. In "Sharh al-Ashbah" by al-Biri: Is it permissible for a person to act on a weak narration concerning himself? Yes, if he has an opinion. As for a layman, I have not seen it, but the implication of restricting it to one with an opinion is that it is not permissible for a layman. He said in "Khizanat al-Riwayat": The scholar who knows the meaning of texts and reports and is among the people of insight may act upon them, even if it contradicts his madhhab. And its restriction to one with an opinion, i.e., the mujtahid within the madhhab, excludes the layman as he said, for he must follow what they have authenticated, except in a place of necessity as you know earlier. If you say: This contradicts what I previously presented that the mujtahid mufti may not deviate from what Abu Hanifa and his companions agreed upon, so he may not give fatwa with it even if he is a perfected mujtahid, because they knew the evidences and distinguished between what is authentic and established and what is not, and his ijtihad does not reach their ijtihad as we previously mentioned from "al-Khaniyyah" and others. I say: That is concerning one who gives fatwa to others. Perhaps its rationale is that since he knows their ijtihad is stronger, he may not build the issues of the laymen on his weaker ijtihad, or because the questioner came only to ask him about the madhhab of the Imam whom that mufti follows, so he must give fatwa according to the madhhab about which the questioner came to ask. Hence, Allamah Qasim mentioned in his fatawa that he was asked about a waqif who stipulated for himself change and substitution, and he made the waqf for his wife. He answered: I have not come across consideration of this in any of the books of our scholars, and the mufti has only to transmit what is authentic according to the people of his madhhab whose statements are used for fatwa; and because the questioner asks only about what the imams of that madhhab held, not about what is clear to the mufti. Similarly, they transmitted from the imams of the Shafi'is that when someone came to ask him about the sale of a heap [of grain], he would say to him: Do you ask me about my madhhab or the madhhab of al-Shafi'i? And similarly they transmitted from him that he sometimes said: If I were to exercise ijtihad and my ijtihad led to the madhhab of Abu Hanifa, I would say the madhhab of al-Shafi'i is such, but I say the madhhab of Abu Hanifa; because he came to learn and ask about the madhhab of al-Shafi'i, so I must inform him that I give fatwa by other than it. As for acting upon it for himself, apparently it is permissible for him, and the statement of "Khizanat al-Riwayat" indicates it: He may act upon them even if it contradicts his madhhab. That is because the mujtahid must follow what his ijtihad leads to. Hence you see the muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam chose issues outside the madhhab, and once he preferred in an issue the statement of Imam Malik and said: This is what I adhere to. And we have previously mentioned from "al-Tahrir" that the mujtahid in some issues, according to the statement of the division of ijtihad which is the truth, must follow [taqlid] in what he is not capable of, i.e., in what he is not capable of ijtihad, not in other matters.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule from the Hanafi usul al-iftaa tradition, addressing the conditions under which a scholar may act on weak (da'if) narrations. It opens by posing the question: can a person act on a weak narration for himself? The answer is yes, provided he has 'ra'y' (insight/opinion), meaning he is a mujtahid. A layman (ammi) lacks this capacity and must follow the authenticated positions of the madhhab. The text then cites Khizanat al-Riwayat, affirming that a scholar who understands texts and is ahl al-dirayah (possessing methodological expertise) may act on weak narrations even if they contradict his madhhab—but this is for personal practice only. The key distinction is between personal 'amal (action) and ifta' (fatwa). When giving fatwa, the mufti must adhere to the established madhhab positions (what Abu Hanifa and his companions agreed upon) because the questioner seeks the madhhab's ruling, not the mufti's personal ijtihad. The rationale is that the ijtihad of the early imams is stronger and more reliable; the mufti's personal ijtihad is weaker and cannot override their consensus. The passage supports this with an anecdote from the Shafi'i school, where a mufti would clarify which madhhab he was following. Finally, it reiterates that for personal practice, a mujtahid may follow weak narrations, as seen in Ibn al-Humam's preference of Malik's opinion. The authority weight of these rulings is from later works like Sharh al-Ashbah and Khizanat al-Riwayat, not the foundational Zahir al-Riwayah, reflecting the fatwa and mutakhkhirin tradition.

Key Terms
العمل بالضعيف (al-'amal bi-al-da'if): Acting upon a weak (da'if) narration in religious practice
العامي (al-'ammi): A layperson who lacks the ability to evaluate narrations or perform ijtihad
المجتهد في المذهب (al-mujtahid fi al-madhhab): A scholar capable of ijtihad within the Hanafi madhhab, but not necessarily an absolute mujtahid
ذي الرأي (dhu al-ra'y): One who possesses juristic insight, i.e., a mujtahid capable of deeming weak narrations acceptable

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why must a mujtahid mufti not deviate from the agreed-upon positions of Abu Hanifa and his companions when giving fatwa?
A) Because the mufti's ijtihad is weaker than the ijtihad of the early imams.
B) Because the questioner only wants the ruling of the madhhab, not the mufti's personal opinion.
C) Both A and B.
D) None of the above.

Key Takeaway
A mujtahid may act on weak narrations for his own practice, but when giving fatwa, he must adhere to the madhhab's established rulings, as the questioner seeks the madhhab's position and the early imams' ijtihad is stronger.

Conditions for Acting on Weak Transmissions (Da'if Riwayat)
Discusses when a mufti or mujtahid may act on weak transmissions within the madhhab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a Hanafi mufti may act on weak transmissions and apply the rasm al-mufti rule to distinguish between personal practice and fatwa-giving.

Core Idea
A mufti may act on a weak transmission for himself if his ijtihad leads to it, but when giving fatwa, he must clarify his madhhab.

This passage from Rasm al-Mufti addresses a nuanced issue: when can a mufti or mujtahid rely on a weaker transmission within the madhhab? The key distinction lies between acting for oneself and issuing a fatwa to others. Understanding this boundary is essential for correct iftaa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage contrasts acting on weak transmissions for personal practice versus giving fatwa to a seeker from a different madhhab. Examine the language for each case.
2
Compare the Hanafi and Shafi'i approaches
Note how Shafi'i imams would respond when the seeker follows a different madhhab. What is the Hanafi alternative? How does al-Qaffal's anecdote illustrate transparency?
3
Analyze the evidence from Khizanat al-Riwayat
The quote permits acting on weak transmissions for oneself. Why does the mujtahid's ijtihad obligate this? Consider the example of Ibn al-Humam.
4
Apply the principle of partial ijtihad
The passage cites al-Tahrir: a partial mujtahid must do taqlid in areas he cannot perform ijtihad. How does this constraint affect the ruling?
5
Formulate the rasm al-mufti rule
Synthesize: when can a mufti act on a weak transmission? When can he give fatwa based on it? State the rule clearly.

شرائط العمل بالضعيف
أئمة الشافعية: أنه كان إذا جاء أحد ذلك المذهب، لا عما ينجلي للمفتي". وكذا نقلوا عن القفال من يستفتيه عن بيع الصبرة يقول له: تسألني عن مذهبي أو عن مذهب الشافعي؟ وكذا نقلوا عنه أنه كان أحيانا يقول: لو اجتهدت فأدى اجتهادي إلى مذهب أبي حنيفة، فأقول : مذهب الشافعي كذا، ولكنّي أقول مذهب أبي حنيفة؛ لأنه جاء ليعلم ويستفتي عن مذهب الشافعي، فلا بد أن أعرفه بأني أفتي بغيره.
وأما في حق العمل به لنفسه فالظاهر جوازه له، ويدل عليه قول "خزانة الروايات": يجوز له أن يعمل عليها وإن كان مخالفا لمذهبه". أي لأن المجتهد يلزمه اتباع ما أدى إليه اجتهاده، ولذا ترى المحقق ابن الهمام اختار مسائل خارجة عن المذهب، ومرّة رجّح في مسألة قول الإمام مالك، وقال: هذا الذي أدين به". وقدمنا عن "التحرير" "أن المجتهد في بعض المسائل على القول بتجزئ الاجتهاد وهو الحق يلزمه التقليد فيما لا يقدر عليه أي فيما لا يقدر على الاجتهاد فيه لا في غيره.
Conditions for acting on the weak (transmission): The imams of the Shafi'is: that when someone from that madhhab came to seek a fatwa, he would not judge by that which became clear to the mufti. They also transmitted from al-Qaffal that someone asked him about the sale of a heap (sabra), and he said: Are you asking me about my madhhab or the madhhab of al-Shafi'i? They also transmitted that he sometimes said: If I exercised ijtihad and my ijtihad led to the madhhab of Abu Hanifa, I would say: The madhhab of al-Shafi'i is such, but I say the madhhab of Abu Hanifa, because he came to learn and seek a fatwa about the madhhab of al-Shafi'i, so I must inform him that I give fatwa by something else. As for acting on it for himself, the apparent is its permissibility for him. And that is indicated by the statement of Khizanat al-Riwayat: 'It is permissible for him to act upon them (weak transmissions) even if they contradict his madhhab.' That is because the mujtahid must follow what his ijtihad leads to. Hence you see the muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam chose issues outside the madhhab, and once he preferred the statement of Imam Malik in an issue and said: 'This is what I adhere to as my religion.' And we previously mentioned from al-Tahrir that the partial mujtahid (on the view allowing partial ijtihad, which is the truth) must do taqlid in what he cannot do ijtihad in, i.e., not in other matters.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti rule concerning the conditions for acting on weak (da'if) transmissions within a madhhab. The author begins by citing the practice of some Shafi'i scholars: when asked for a fatwa, they would clarify that they are giving fatwa according to their own madhhab even if their personal ijtihad leads elsewhere. Then he distinguishes between acting for oneself and giving fatwa to others: it is permissible for a mujtahid to act on a weak transmission for himself, even if it contradicts his madhhab, because his ijtihad obligates him to follow what it leads to. Evidence is given from Khizanat al-Riwayat and the example of Ibn al-Humam. Finally, the passage cites al-Tahrir on partial ijtihad: a mujtahid in some issues must do taqlid in areas where he cannot perform ijtihad, but not in matters he can.

Key Terms
الضعيف (al-da'if): A weak transmission (riwaya) within the madhhab that is not the strongest or most relied-upon opinion.
المجتهد (al-mujtahid): A scholar capable of deriving rulings from primary sources; here referring to a partial mujtahid who can perform ijtihad in some issues.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is permissible, as indicated by Khizanat al-Riwayat.
C) It is wajib to act on the strongest opinion.
D) It is only permitted for the mufti, not the layman.

Key Takeaway
A mufti may act on weak transmissions for his personal practice if his ijtihad leads to it, but when giving fatwa he must uphold the predominant view of his madhhab and be transparent with the seeker.

Ruling with Weak Opinions and Opinions of Other Schools
Rasm al-mufti rule on judge's use of weak and cross-madhhab opinions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a Hanafi judge may rule using a weak opinion or another school's opinion, and apply the preponderant (mufta bihi) position regarding the judge's adherence to his madhhab.

Core Idea
A muqallid judge must judge by his madhhab's relied-upon view; deviation invalidates the ruling.

This lesson examines a key rasm al-mufti rule: when may a judge rule using a weak opinion within his madhhab or an opinion from another school? The passage distinguishes between mujtahid and muqallid judges, and presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf about the validity of rulings that deviate from the judge's own ijtihad. Understanding this distinction is crucial for ensuring the integrity of qada' and fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of judges
Note the mujtahid vs muqallid distinction: a mujtahid is qualified for independent reasoning, while a muqallid follows a specific madhhab.
The passage defines the scope for each.
2
Extract the rule for each category
A mujtahid must judge by his own preponderant (rajih) opinion. A muqallid may judge by the well-known (mashhur) opinion of his madhhab, even if not personally preponderant.
This is derived from the answer to Ibn Idris's question.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Examine the case of a mujtahid judge who rules contrary to his ijtihad: Abu Hanifa allows execution if forgetful (two narrations for intentional), while the Sahibayn hold it invalid in both cases.
The passage cites sources like al-Khaniyya and al-Muhit.
4
Determine the tarjih (preferred view)
Later authorities like Fath al-Qadir prefer the Sahibayn's view due to concern for desire (hawa) and the nature of judicial appointment.
This is the mufta bihi for contemporary practice.
5
Apply to the muqallid judge
A muqallid judge has no flexibility; he must judge strictly by the madhhab of Abu Hanifa as appointed. Any deviation renders the ruling invalid and the judge effectively removed from office for that case.
This reinforces the strict binding of the muqallid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القضاء بالضعيف وبمذهب الغير
وقولي لكنما القاضي به لا يقضي إلخ أي لا يقضي بالضعيف من مذهبه وكذا بمذهب الغير.
قال العلامة قاسم وقال أبو العباس أحمد بن إدريس: هل يجب على الحاكم أن لا يحكم إلا بالراجح عنده، كما يجب على المفتي أن لا يفتي إلا بالراجح عنده، أو له أن يحكم بأحد القولين، وإن لم يكن راجحاً عنده؟ جوابه: أن الحاكم إن كان مجتهدا، فلا يجوز أن يحكم ويفتي إلا بالراجح عنده، وإن كان مقلّدا جاز له أن يفتي بالمشهور في مذهبه، وأن يحكم به، وإن لم يكن راجحاً عنده، مقلّدا في رجحان المحكوم به إمامه الذي يقلّده، كما يقلّده في الفتوى وأما اتباع الهوى في الحكم والفتيا فحرام إجماعا. وأما الحكم والفتيا لما هو مرجوح فخلاف الإجماع". وذكر في "البحر": لو قضى في المجتهد فيه مخالفاً لرأيه، ناسياً لمذهبه، نفذ عند أبي حنيفة وفي العامد روايتان وعندهما: لا ينفذ في الوجهين. واختلف الترجيح، ففي "الخانية" : أظهر الروايتين عن أبي حنيفة نفاذ قضائه وعليه الفتوى، وهكذا في الفتاوى الصغرى. وفي "المعراج" معزياً إلى "المحيط: الفتوى على قولهما، وهكذا في "الهداية". وفي "فتح القدير": فقد اختلف في الفتوى والوجه في هذا الزمان أن يفتى بقولهما؛ لأن التارك لمذهبه عمداً لا يفعله إلا لهوى باطل، لا لقصد جميل، وأما الناسي؛ فلأن المقلد ما قلّده إلا ليحكم بمذهبه لا بمذهب غيره. هذا كله في القاضي المجتهد، فأما المقلّد، فإنما وَلَّاه ليحكم بمذهب أبي حنيفة، فلا يملك المخالفة، فيكون معزولاً بالنسبة إلى هذا الحكم".انتهى ما في "الفتح"، انتهى كلام "البحر".
Ruling with the weak (opinion) and with the opinion of another school. And my statement: 'But the judge, by it, does not judge, etc.' meaning he does not judge by the weak from his madhhab, nor by the opinion of another school. Allamah Qasim said: And Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Idris said: Is it obligatory upon the judge that he should not judge except by the preponderant (rajih) in his view, just as it is obligatory upon the mufti not to give fatwa except by the preponderant in his view? Or may he judge by one of the two opinions even if it is not preponderant in his view? The answer: If the judge is a mujtahid, it is not permissible for him to judge or give fatwa except by the preponderant in his view. If he is a muqallid, it is permissible for him to give fatwa by the well-known (mashhur) in his madhhab and to judge by it, even if it is not preponderant in his view, as a muqallid in the preponderance of the ruling of his imam whom he follows, just as he follows him in fatwa. As for following desire in judgment and fatwa, it is haram by consensus. And judgment and fatwa by a preponderated (marjuh) opinion is contrary to consensus. And it is mentioned in al-Bahr: If he judged in a matter open to ijtihad in opposition to his own opinion, forgetting his madhhab, it is executable according to Abu Hanifa. And in the case of intentional (contradiction), there are two narrations. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is not executable in both cases. The tarjih (preference) differed. In al-Khaniyya: The more apparent of the two narrations from Abu Hanifa is that his judgment is executable, and that is what the fatwa is upon, and likewise in al-Fatawa al-Sughra. In al-Mi'raj quoting al-Muhit: The fatwa is upon their (the two's) statement, and likewise in al-Hidaya. In Fath al-Qadir: There is disagreement in the fatwa, and the view in this time is that fatwa is given by their statement, because one who intentionally leaves his madhhab does so only for base desire, not for a good purpose. As for the forgetful, because the muqallid only made him a judge to judge by his madhhab, not by another's madhhab. All this is regarding the mujtahid judge. As for the muqallid, he was appointed to judge by the madhhab of Abu Hanifa, so he does not have the power to oppose, and he is effectively removed (from office) with respect to this ruling. End of what is in al-Fath. End of the words of al-Bahr.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti rule concerning the judge's (qadi) use of weak opinions within his madhhab or opinions from another school. It begins with a quote from the author's prior statement that the judge should not judge by weak opinions or by another school. Then it presents a question from Ahmad ibn Idris: must a judge only rule by the preponderant opinion, or can he use a non-preponderant one? The answer distinguishes between a mujtahid judge (must follow his own ijtihad) and a muqallid judge (may follow the mashhur of his madhhab even if not personally preponderant). Following desire is unanimously forbidden. Then the passage cites al-Bahr on a specific case: if a mujtahid judge rules contrary to his view while forgetting his madhhab, it is executable according to Abu Hanifa; but if intentional, there are two narrations. The Sahibayn hold it not executable in either case. There is a difference in tarjih: some sources favor Abu Hanifa, others favor the Sahibayn. The passage concludes that the muqallid judge cannot deviate from his madhhab at all, and doing so would be ultra vires.

Key Terms
الضعيف (al-da'if): A weak opinion within the madhhab that is not the preponderant (rajih) view.
المجتهد (al-mujtahid): A judge who is qualified to perform ijtihad and is bound by his own ijtihad in rulings.
المقلد (al-muqallid): A judge who does not reach the level of ijtihad and must follow a specific madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) His ruling is always valid.
B) His ruling is invalid according to the Sahibayn, and there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa.
C) His ruling is valid only if he is forgetful.
D) His ruling is valid regardless of intention.

Key Takeaway
A judge's authority is bounded by his level of ijtihad; a muqallid must judge only by the preponderant opinion of his madhhab, and even a mujtahid risks invalidating his ruling if he deviates intentionally.

8 min
Non-Enforceability of Ruling by Weak Opinion
Resolving the ikhtilaf on a muqallid judge's ruling by weak opinion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that a muqallid judge's judgment by a weak (marjuh) or non-madhhab opinion is void and subject to reversal, and identify the key maxim and authorities that support this position.

Core Idea
A muqallid judge's ruling by a weak opinion is void; the weak is like non-existent.

This passage resolves a critical debate within the Hanafi school: can a muqallid judge rule by a weak opinion (marjuh) or by the opinion of another madhhab? The early mashayikh differed, but the later relied-upon authorities (mutakhkhirin) decisively hold that such rulings do not take effect and can be overturned. This lesson unpacks the evidence, the maxim 'the weak opinion is like non-existence', and the practical implications for judicial practice today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The passage reports two views: (1) some early scholars (e.g., in al-Bazzaziyya) held the ruling is effective (nafidh); (2) the majority and later authorities hold it is not effective.
The first view is based on a transmission from Imam Muhammad, but it is considered a rare riwaya.
2
Analyze the relied-upon position
The text affirms the position in Fath al-Qadir, al-Nahr, al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and Fatawa Qasim: the ruling does not take effect and is overturned.
This is the mufta bihi position for fatwa and qada.
3
Apply the maxim
The maxim 'the weak opinion is in the status of non-existence alongside the preponderant' (القول المرجوح بمنزلة العدم مع الراجح) is cited. For the muqallid judge, if a rajih opinion exists, the marjuh is effectively void, so ruling by it is like ruling by nothing.
This maxim is a dabt (sub-maxim) under the broader principle of taqlid.
4
Consider additional factors
In contemporary times, the sultan's decree often prohibits judging by weak opinions, reinforcing the ruling. Even without such a decree, the muqallid judge is bound by the rajih.
The judge's mandate is specific to the madhhab's preponderant views.
5
Conclude the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a judge rules by a weak opinion, the ruling is not final; it can be overturned by another judge or by appeal. The judge who issued it may also reverse it (as per the early view), but the stronger position holds it is automatically void.
This protects the integrity of the madhhab and prevents arbitrary judgments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم ذكر أنه اختلفت عبارات المشايخ في القاضي المقلد، والذي عليه كلامه أنه إذا قضى بمذهب غيره، أو برواية ضعيفة، أو بقول ضعيف، نفذ. وأقوى ما تمسك به، ما في "البزازية" عن "شرح الطحاوي" إذا لم يكن القاضي مجتهداً، وقضى بالفتوى، ثم تبين أنه على خلاف مذهبه نفذ، وليس لغيره نقضه، وله أن ينقضه، كذا عن محمد. وقال الثاني: ليس له أن ينقضه أيضا. لكنّ الذي في "القنية" عن "المحيط" وغيره أن اختلاف الروايات في قاض مجتهد إذا قضى على خلاف رأيه، والقاضي المقلّد إذا قضى على خلاف مذهبه لا ينفذ. وبه جزم المحقق في "فتح القدير"، وتلميذه العلامة قاسم في تصحيحه. قال في "النهر": وما في "الفتح": يجب أن يعوّل عليه في المذهب، وما في "البزازية" محمول على رواية عنهما، فصار الأمر أن هذا منزّل منزلة الناسي لمذهبه، وقد مرّ عنهما في المجتهد أنه لا ينفذ، فالمقلد أولى. وقال في "الدر المختار": قلت: ولا سيّما في زماننا، فإن السلطان ينص في منشوره على نهيه عن القضاء بالأقوال الضعيفة، فكيف بخلاف مذهبه؟ فيكون معزولاً بالنسبة لغير المعتمد من مذهبه، فلا ينفذ قضاؤه فيه، وينقض كما بسط في قضاء "الفتح" و"البحر" و"النهر" وغيرها. قلت: وقد علمت أيضاً أن القول المرجوح بمنزلة العدم مع الراجح، فليس له الحكم به وإن لم ينص له السلطان على الحكم بالراجح. وفي "فتاوى العلامة قاسم: وليس للقاضي المقلّد أن يحكم بالضعيف؛
Then he mentioned that the expressions of the mashayikh differed regarding the muqallid judge. The apparent meaning of his words is that if he judges by the opinion of another madhhab, or by a weak narration, or by a weak saying, it is effective. And the strongest thing they hold onto is what is in 'al-Bazzaziyya' from 'Sharh al-Tahawi': if the judge is not a mujtahid, and he judges by a fatwa, then it becomes clear that it is contrary to his madhhab, it is effective, and no one else may overturn it, but he may overturn it. This is from Muhammad. And the second said: He may not overturn it either. But that which is in 'al-Qunya' from 'al-Muhit' and others is that the difference of narrations is: in a mujtahid judge, if he judges contrary to his opinion, and in a muqallid judge, if he judges contrary to his madhhab, it does not take effect. And the muhaqqiq in 'Fath al-Qadir' and his student 'Allama Qasim in his correction affirmed this. He said in 'al-Nahr': What is in 'al-Fath' must be relied upon in the madhhab, and what is in 'al-Bazzaziyya' is carried upon a narration from them. So the matter is that this is considered like the one who forgets his madhhab, and it has already been mentioned from them (the two companions) regarding the mujtahid that it does not take effect, so the muqallid is even more so. And he said in 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar': I say: especially in our time, for the sultan states in his decree his prohibition of judging by weak opinions, so how about (judging) contrary to his madhhab? So he is removed with respect to what is not relied upon from his madhhab, so his judgment in it does not take effect, and it is overturned, as explained in the section on judging in 'al-Fath', 'al-Bahr', 'al-Nahr', and others. I say: And I have also learned that the weak opinion is in the status of non-existence alongside the preponderant, so he may not judge by it even if the sultan did not instruct him to judge by the preponderant. And in 'Fatawa al-'Allama Qasim': And it is not for the muqallid judge to judge by the weak;
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a legal refinement regarding the enforceability of a muqallid judge's ruling when he uses a weak opinion (da'if) within his madhhab or an opinion from another madhhab. The author reports that the early mashayikh differed: some, citing 'al-Bazzaziyya' from 'Sharh al-Tahawi' and a transmission from Imam Muhammad, held that such a ruling is effective (nafidh) and cannot be overturned by others, though the judge himself could reverse it. However, the stronger and later relied-upon position, as affirmed in 'Fath al-Qadir', 'al-Nahr', 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar', and others, is that the ruling is not effective. The reasoning is that the muqallid judge is appointed specifically to judge by the Hanafi madhhab, and if he deviates intentionally or through a weak opinion, he is effectively removed from office for that judgment. Moreover, the weak opinion (marjuh) is considered as non-existent when a preponderant opinion exists. In our time, the sultan's decree often explicitly prohibits judging by weak opinions, reinforcing this ruling. Thus, the muqallid judge's judgment by a weak or foreign opinion is void and subject to reversal.

Key Terms
مقلّد (muqallid): A judge who does not have ijtihad and follows the rulings of a specific madhhab (here, Hanafi).
نفوذ (nafadh): Legal effectiveness and enforceability of a judicial ruling.
ضعيف (da'if): A weak opinion within the madhhab, outweighed by a stronger (rajih) opinion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a muqallid judge who intentionally judges by a weak opinion (marjuh) within his madhhab, according to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position?
A) The judgment is effective and binding.
B) The judgment is not effective and will be overturned.
C) The judgment is effective only if the sultan does not prohibit it.
D) The judgment is effective only if the judge later confirms it.

Key Takeaway
A muqallid judge's ruling by a weak or non-madhhab opinion is void and must be overturned because the weak opinion is legally non-existent alongside the preponderant.

Non-Enforceability of a Muqallid Qadi's Ruling
Rule on enforceability of a muqallid qadi's ruling against his madhhab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on the enforceability of a muqallid qadi's ruling and evaluate the conflicting opinions to identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A muqallid qadi's ruling contrary to his madhhab is void; he must follow the strong opinion only.

This passage addresses a critical issue in judicial practice: what happens when a non-mujtahid judge issues a ruling that contradicts the relied-upon opinions of his own school? While some early sources held such rulings enforceable, the established Hanafi position firmly rejects them. Understanding this rule is essential for anyone involved in fatwa or qada.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central issue
The issue is whether a muqallid qadi's ruling based on a weak narration or another madhhab is legally enforceable. Two conflicting positions exist.
2
Examine each position
Position 1 (from al-Bazzaziyya): enforceable, only the qadi may overturn it. Position 2 (from al-Qunyah, Fath al-Qadir): not enforceable, any party may seek overturn.
3
Analyze the reasoning for the mu'tamad view
The mu'tamad view argues that a muqallid is not qualified for tarjih, so he must adhere to the strong (rajih) opinion. A weak opinion is like non-existent; ruling by it is judging without truth.
This reasoning is supported by Fath al-Qadir, al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and Fatawa Qasim.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
Under the enforceable view, the ruling stands unless the qadi overturns it. Under the mu'tamad view, the ruling is void and any party can have it overturned.
5
Apply the tarjih mechanism
The Bazzaziyya view is based on a weak riwaya; later scholars (Ibn Humam, Ibn Abidin) have settled on the non-enforceable view as the mufta bihi.
This is consistent with the principle that later tarjih relies on stronger evidence and usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم ذكر أنه اختلفت عبارات المشايخ في القاضي المقلد، والذي عليه كلامه أنه إذا قضى بمذهب غيره، أو برواية ضعيفة، أو بقول ضعيف، نفذ. وأقوى ما تمسك به، ما في "البزازية" عن "شرح الطحاوي" إذا لم يكن القاضي مجتهداً، وقضى بالفتوى، ثم تبين أنه على خلاف مذهبه نفذ، وليس لغيره نقضه، وله أن ينقضه، كذا عن محمد. وقال الثاني: ليس له أن ينقضه أيضا". لكنّ الذي في "القنية" عن "المحيط" وغيره أن اختلاف الروايات في قاض مجتهد إذا قضى على خلاف رأيه، والقاضي المقلّد إذا قضى على خلاف مذهبه لا ينفذ. وبه جزم المحقق في "فتح القدير"، وتلميذه العلامة قاسم في تصحيحه. قال في "النهر": وما في "الفتح": يجب أن يعوّل عليه في المذهب، وما في "البزازية" محمول على رواية عنهما، فصار الأمر أن هذا منزّل منزلة الناسي لمذهبه، وقد مرّ عنهما في المجتهد أنه لا ينفذ، فالمقلد أولى. وقال في "الدر المختار": قلت: ولا سيّما في زماننا، فإن السلطان ينص في منشوره على نهيه عن القضاء بالأقوال الضعيفة، فكيف بخلاف مذهبه؟ فيكون معزولاً بالنسبة لغير المعتمد من مذهبه، فلا ينفذ قضاؤه فيه، وينقض كما بسط في قضاء "الفتح" و"البحر" و"النهر" وغيرها. قلت: وقد علمت أيضاً أن القول المرجوح بمنزلة العدم مع الراجح، فليس له الحكم به وإن لم ينص له السلطان على الحكم بالراجح. وفي "فتاوى العلامة قاسم": وليس للقاضي المقلّد أن يحكم بالضعيف؛ لأنه ليس من أهل الترجيح، فلا يعدل عن الصحيح إلا لقصد غير جميل، ولو حكم لا ينفذ؛ لأن قضاءه قضاء بغير الحق؛ لأن الحق هو الصحيح. وما نقل من أن القول الضعيف يتقوّى بالقضاء المراد به قضاء المجتهد، كما بيّن في موضعه مما لا يحتمله هذا الجواب. وما ذكره من هذا المراد صرّح به شيخه المحقق في "فتح القدير". وهذا آخر ما أردنا إيراده من التقرير والتوضيح والتحرير، بعون الله تعالى العليم الخبير. أسأله سبحانه أن يجعل ذلك خالصاً لوجهه الكريم، موجباً للفوز لديه يوم الموقف العظيم. وأن يعفو عمّا جَنَيتُه واقترفته من خطأ وأوزار فإنه العزيز الغفار والحمد لله تعالى أولاً وآخراً وظاهراً وباطناً. والحمد لله الذي بنعمته تتم الصالحات. وصلّى الله تعالى على سيدنا محمد وعلى آله وصحبه وسلم، والحمد لله رب العالمين. نجز ذلك بقلم جامعه الفقير محمد عابدين غفر الله تعالى له ولوالديه ومشايخه وذريته والمسلمين آمين. وذلك في شهر ربيع الثاني سنة ثلاث وأربعين ومائتين وألف.
Then he mentioned that the statements of the mashayikh differed concerning the muqallid qadi. According to his own discussion, if he judges according to another madhhab, or by a weak narration, or by a weak opinion, it is enforceable. The strongest thing held is what is in al-Bazzaziyya from Sharh al-Tahawi: if the qadi is not a mujtahid and judges by a fatwa, then it becomes clear that it is against his madhhab, it is enforceable, and no one else may overturn it, but he himself may overturn it—thus from Muhammad. The second said: he cannot overturn it either. However, what is in al-Qunyah from al-Muhit and others is that if a mujtahid qadi rules against his own opinion, or a muqallid qadi rules against his madhhab, it is not enforceable. And the muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir and his student Allamah Qasim confirmed this. He said in al-Nahr: What is in al-Fath must be relied upon in the madhhab, and what is in al-Bazzaziyya is carried on a riwaya from them both. Thus the matter is that this is treated like one who forgot his madhhab, and it has already passed from them both regarding the mujtahid that it is not enforceable, so the muqallid is more so. And he said in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: I say: especially in our time, for the sultan states in his decree his prohibition of judging by weak opinions, how much more so against his madhhab? Thus he is dismissed regarding non-mu'tamad parts of his madhhab, so his ruling therein is not enforceable, and it is overturned as elaborated in Qada of al-Fath, al-Bahr, al-Nahr, and others. I say: It is also known that the marjuh opinion is like non-existent alongside the rajih, so he may not judge by it even if the sultan has not prescribed judgment by the rajih. In Fatawa al-Allamah Qasim: The muqallid qadi may not judge by the weak, because he is not among those qualified for tarjih, so he does not deviate from the sahih except for an unseemly purpose, and if he judges it is not enforceable, because his judgment is judgment without truth, for the truth is the sahih. And what is transmitted that a weak opinion is strengthened by being used in a ruling—the intended meaning is the ruling of a mujtahid, as explained in its place, which this answer cannot bear. And what he mentioned about this meaning was explicitly stated by his teacher the muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir. This is the extent of what we intended to present of explanation, elucidation, and correction, with the help of Allah, the All-Knowing, the All-Aware. I ask Him the Exalted to make it purely for His noble face, and a cause for success with Him on the great Day of Standing. And to forgive what I have committed and perpetrated of error and burdens, for He is the Mighty, the Forgiving. And praise be to Allah first and last, outwardly and inwardly. And praise be to Allah by whose grace good deeds are completed. And may Allah send blessings upon our master Muhammad and his family and companions and grant them peace. And praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds. It was completed by the pen of its compiler, the poor Muhammad Abidin, may Allah forgive him, his parents, his teachers, his offspring, and the Muslims, Amen. This was in the month of Rabi al-Thani in the year 1243.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a rule (rasm al-mufti) concerning the enforceability of a muqallid qadi's ruling when it contradicts his own madhhab or relies on a weak opinion. The author presents the ikhtilaf among mashayikh. Some, based on al-Bazzaziyya, hold that such a ruling is enforceable and can only be overturned by the qadi himself. Others, from al-Qunyah and al-Muhit, assert it is not enforceable at all. The author sides with the latter, considered the relied-upon position (mu'tamad), citing Fath al-Qadir and al-Durr al-Mukhtar. The key reasoning: a muqallid is not qualified for tarjih, so he must stick to the strong opinion (rajih) of his madhhab. Judging by a weak or contrary opinion is equivalent to judging without truth, hence the ruling is void. The sultan's decree further prohibits such practices. The passage concludes with Ibn Abidin's supplication.

Key Terms
قاضي مقلد (qāḍī muqallid): A judge who is not a mujtahid and follows a particular madhhab in his rulings.
رواية ضعيفة (riwāya ḍaʿīfa): A transmitted opinion within the Hanafi school that is considered weak or less authoritative.
قول مرجوح (qawl marjūḥ): An opinion that is outweighed by a stronger (rajih) opinion within the school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon opinion in the Hanafi school, what is the status of a muqallid qadi's ruling when he judges by a weak opinion in his own madhhab?
A) It is enforceable and cannot be overturned by anyone.
B) It is enforceable but the qadi himself may overturn it.
C) It is not enforceable and must be overturned.
D) It is enforceable only if the sultan permits it.

Key Takeaway
A muqallid qadi's ruling that contradicts the relied-upon opinion of his madhhab is void and must be overturned; he is bound to follow only the strong opinion.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Non-enforceability of a Judge's Ruling Based on a Weak Opinion
Final ruling on a judge's capacity to rule by a weak opinion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a non-mujtahid judge's ruling based on a weak opinion is invalid and unenforceable, and distinguish the case of a mujtahid judge.

Core Idea
A non-mujtahid judge's ruling on a weak opinion is void; only a mujtahid's ruling can strengthen a marjuh view.

This passage from a late Hanafi commentary clarifies a critical rule in the mufti's craft: a judge who is not qualified to weigh evidence (tarjih) cannot deviate from the sahih (correct) opinion. If he does, his ruling has no legal effect. This principle is foundational for understanding the hierarchy of juridical authority and the conditions for enforceable judgments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actor and the act
The passage discusses a judge (qadi) issuing a ruling based on a weak (marjuh) opinion. First, note who the judge is: the text says he is 'not from the people of tarjih' (laysa min ahl al-tarjih).
This implies the judge is a muqallid, not a mujtahid.
2
Assess the judge's qualification
Understand what 'not from the people of tarjih' means: the judge lacks the ability to weigh evidence and determine the stronger opinion. He must follow the established correct view (sahih).
Tarjih is a specific skill of the mujtahid.
3
Apply the rule
The passage rules that such a judge's ruling based on a weak opinion does not execute (la yanfudh). The reason: his judgment is 'without truth' (bi ghayr al-haqq) because the truth is the sahih.
Thus, the ruling is legally void.
4
Note the exception
The text mentions a narration that 'a weak opinion becomes strong by a judge's ruling', but clarifies this applies only to a mujtahid judge, not a muqallid.
This prevents misinterpretation of the principle.
5
Recognize the conclusion
The author concludes that the correct position (mufta bihi) is that a non-mujtahid's ruling on a weak opinion is unenforceable. The commentary ends with a prayer.
This is a settled rule in Hanafi ifta.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عدم نفاذ القضاء بمذهب الغير لأنه ليس من أهل الترجيح، فلا يعدل عن الصحيح إلا لقصد غير جميل، ولو حكم لا ينفذ؛ لأن قضاءه قضاء بغير الحق؛ لأن الحق هو الصحيح. وما نقل من أن القول الضعيف يتقوّى بالقضاء المراد به قضاء المجتهد، كما بيّن في موضعه مما لا يحتمله هذا الجواب. وما ذكره من هذا المراد صرّح به شيخه المحقق في "فتح القدير". وهذا آخر ما أردنا إيراده من التقرير والتوضيح والتحرير، بعون الله تعالى العليم الخبير. أسأله سبحانه أن يجعل ذلك خالصاً لوجهه الكريم، موجباً للفوز لديه يوم الموقف العظيم. وأن يعفو عمّا جَنَيتُه واقترفته من خطأ وأوزار فإنه العزيز الغفار والحمد لله تعالى أولاً وآخراً وظاهراً وباطناً. والحمد لله الذي بنعمته تتم الصالحات. وصلّى الله تعالى على سيدنا محمد وعلى آله وصحبه وسلم، والحمد لله رب العالمين. نجز ذلك بقلم جامعه الفقير محمد عابدين غفر الله تعالى له ولوالديه ومشايخه وذريته والمسلمين آمين. وذلك في شهر ربيع الثاني سنة ثلاث وأربعين ومائتين وألف.
The non-enforceability of a judge's ruling according to another's madhhab because he is not one of those qualified for tarjih (preference), so he should not deviate from the sahih (correct) except for an ignoble purpose. And if he judges, it is not enforceable; because his judgment is a judgment without truth; because the truth is the sahih. And what is narrated that a weak opinion becomes strong by a judge's ruling, meaning the ruling of a mujtahid, as clarified in its place, is not borne by this answer. And what he mentioned of this meaning was explicitly stated by his teacher, the muhaqqiq, in 'Fath al-Qadir'. This is the last of what we intended to present of explanation, clarification, and editing, with the help of Allah, the All-Knowing, the All-Aware. I ask Him, the Glorified, to make this purely for His noble countenance, leading to success before Him on the Great Day. And to forgive what I have perpetrated and committed of mistakes and sins, for He is the Mighty, the Forgiver. And praise be to Allah, first and last, outwardly and inwardly. And praise be to Allah, by whose grace good deeds are completed. And may Allah bless our master Muhammad and his family and companions, and praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds. It was completed by the pen of its writer, the poor one, Muhammad Abidin, may Allah forgive him, his parents, his teachers, his offspring, and all Muslims, amen. And that was in the month of Rabi' al-Thani, year 1243 [AH].
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a concluding ruling from the commentary. It addresses the issue of a judge who is not a mujtahid (i.e., not qualified to weigh evidence) issuing a ruling based on a weak or less-preferred opinion. The ruling is clear: such a ruling is unenforceable because the judge is not from the people of tarjih. He should only follow the correct (sahih) view. The text refutes the idea that a weak opinion gains strength simply by being enacted in a judgment, noting that this applies only to mujtahids. The author concludes the commentary with a prayer.

Key Terms
عدم نفاذ (adam nafadh): Non-enforceability; a ruling that has no legal effect.
المرجوح (al-marjuh): The weaker/unpreferred opinion as opposed to the rajih (preferred).
أهل الترجيح (ahl al-tarjih): Those qualified to weigh evidence and determine the stronger opinion; i.e., mujtahids.
الصحيح (al-sahih): The correct, preferred opinion within the madhhab; the truth (haqq).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is a non-mujtahid judge's ruling based on a weak opinion unenforceable?
A) Because the judge is not qualified for tarjih, so his judgment is without truth.
B) Because the ruling is based on a weak opinion, which is always invalid.
C) Because the litigants did not agree to the ruling.
D) Because the judge's ruling was overturned by a higher authority.

Key Takeaway
A non-mujtahid judge's ruling based on a weak opinion is void; only a mujtahid can strengthen a weak opinion through his judgment.
